Altarweej li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
Noble Endorsement
Investigator of the age, emperor of teaching, teacher of scholars, Hazrat Maulana Muhammad Ismail Arshad (may his blessings endure), teacher of hadith at Darul Uloom Kabirwala
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger.
All the books that Allama Taftazani authored are precise, especially al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Our brother in Allah, the virtuous Maulana Muhammad Luqman Jalal Fouri, teacher of hadith at Darul Uloom Kabirwala, has written upon it excellent, beneficial, elegant, complete, and comprehensive annotations for solving the book, with no further addition needed and no need for any other explanation, Allah willing.
By Allah, excellent is what the author has done, for he has striven and exerted his effort. May Allah make it a continuous charity for the author and beneficial for the readers.
Through the rank of the Master of the Messengers.
And may Allah send blessings upon the best of His creation, Muhammad, and upon all his family and companions.
Only peace.
Muhammad Ismail Arshad
/Rabi' al-Akhir, 1432? (date unclear)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage comprises two taqriz (commendations) from esteemed scholars praising the commentary 'Altarweeh li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. The first is by Maulana Mufti Muhammad Hasan, who extols the author Maulana Muhammad Luqman and highlights the importance of protecting the deen. The second is by Maulana Muhammad Ismail Arshad, who notes the precision of Allama Taftazani's original works and praises the valuable annotations of Maulana Muhammad Luqman, calling them complete and sufficient without need for further explanation. This front matter establishes the authority and usefulness of the commentary for students of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
تقریظ (taqriz): A formal scholarly endorsement or commendation, often found at the beginning of a book to certify its quality and authority.
شرح (sharh): A commentary or explanation of a text. Here, 'Altarweeh' is a sharh on 'al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'.
توضیح تلویح (al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih): A famous work on Hanafi usul al-fiqh by Allama Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. It is known for its precision and depth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Maulana Muhammad Ismail Arshad

Key Takeaway
The taqriz authenticate the commentary as a complete, reliable, and sufficient guide to Taftazani's usul al-fiqh, endorsed by respected Hanafi scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Introduction to Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: Scholarly Endorsements and Context
Two scholarly endorsements commending the book and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of the book Al-Tarwih as described in the endorsements and explain its significance in the Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh curriculum.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements authenticate a work and highlight its utility for mastering complex Usul texts.

This lesson begins the study of Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih by presenting two endorsements from prominent scholars. These taqriz not only praise the author but also underscore the importance of Usul al-Fiqh and the difficulty of the original text, al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Understanding this front matter helps you appreciate the purpose and approach of the commentary you are about to study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the endorsers
Find the names of the two scholars who wrote the endorsements (taqriz). Note their credentials and the tone of their praise.
Muhammad Ismail Arshad and Mufti Hamid Hasan both hold teaching positions at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala.
2
Extract the book's purpose
From both endorsements, determine what the book Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih aims to achieve. Look for phrases about solving difficulties, summarizing, or making the text accessible.
The book is described as a solution (hall) to the difficulties of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih.
3
Understand the context of Usul al-Fiqh
Note how Mufti Hamid Hasan explains the importance of Usul al-Fiqh in the Dars Nizami curriculum and why a commentary like this is needed.
He mentions the complexity of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih and the current academic stagnation.
4
Identify the author's methodology
From the endorsements, list the methodological features of the commentary: textual analysis, translation, explanation of objectives, lexical and morphological investigation.
These features make the book comprehensive and beneficial.

اما بعد ! علوم دینیہ میں سے علم اصول فقہ استنباط احکام کیلئے ایک بنیادی حیثیت رکھتا ہے جس کی بدولت قرآن وسنت کا سمجھنا سمجھانا آسان ہو جاتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ حضرات اکابرین رحمہم اللہ نے درس نظامی میں جہاں دوسرے علوم عالیہ وآلیہ کو شامل نصاب کیا وہاں علم اصول فقہ کو بھی اہمیت دیتے ہوئے نصاب کا حصہ بنا یا علم اصول فقہ سے متعلق مختلف کتب درجہ وار پڑھائی جاتی ہیں آجکل وفاق المدارس العربیہ پاکستان کے مجوزہ نصاب میں سب سے اخیر میں پڑھائی جانے والی اصول فقہ کی کتاب التوضیح والتلویح سے فنی اعتبار سے التوضیح والتلویح غامض اور بہت ادق کتاب ہے محقق تفتازانی کی علمی موشگافیان مزید براں ہیں اس نازک اور علمی جمود کے دور میں کتب فنون کو بغیر معاون کے بآسانی پڑھنا پڑھانا انتہائی دشوار ہے
کما ہو المشاہد
کہنہ مشق ماہر استاذ برادرم مولانا محمد لقمان صاحب مدظلہ استاذ الحدیث دارالعلوم کبیر والا نے التوضیح والتلویح کئی مرتبہ پڑھانے کے بعد بطور نچوڑا الترویح لحل التوضیح والتلویح تصنیف فرمائی ہے ماشاء اللہ کتاب اسم باسمی ہے جس میں عبارت کو معرب کرنے کے ساتھ ساتھ ترجمہ اور اغراض شارح کو اچھے اسلوب میں بیان کیا ہے جبکہ مشکل الفاظ کی لغوی و صرفی تحقیق اضافی خوبیوں میں سے ہے امید ہے کہ برادرم موصوف کی یہ علمی کاوش علماء وطلباء ہر دو کیلئے مفید ثابت ہوگی برادرم موصوف نے الترویح لحل التوضیح والتلویح تحریر کر کے دارالعلوم کبیر والا کی تصنیفی کاوشوں میں اضافہ کیا ہے دعا ہے کہ اللہ جل شانہ شرح مذکور کو اور اس سے پہلے شائع کردہ مصباح الحكمة شرح هداية الحكمة کو شرف قبولیت
عطاء فرمائے
آمین بجاہ سید المرسلین
طالب دعا حامد حسن
استاذ دار العلوم عید گاہ کبیروالا ۱۴۳۲٫۵/۱۰ھ
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. All the books authored by the great scholar al-Taftazani are precise, especially al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Our brother in Allah, the virtuous Mawlana Muhammad Luqman Jalal Furi, teacher of Hadith at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, has annotated it with excellent, beneficial, elegant, complete, and comprehensive notes for solving the book. There is nothing beyond it and no need for any other commentary after it, God willing. Allah has rewarded the author for his effort and striving, and may He make it a continuing charity for the author and beneficial for those who study it. By the station of the Master of the Messengers. May Allah bless the best of His creation, Muhammad, and all his family and companions. Only and peace. Muhammad Ismail Arshad. Rabi' al-Akhir, 1432? [date unclear]. Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. [Page 41] A gracious opinion. The teacher of scholars, Hadrat Mawlana Mufti Hamid Hasan Sahib, may his blessings endure, head of ifta' and teacher of Hadith at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala. Muhammad and peace upon his noble Messenger. To proceed: Among the religious sciences, the science of Usul al-Fiqh has a foundational position for deriving rulings, through which understanding and explaining the Quran and Sunnah becomes easy. This is why the great scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) included it in the Dars Nizami curriculum alongside other higher and instrumental sciences, giving importance to Usul al-Fiqh as part of the syllabus. Various books on Usul al-Fiqh are taught in a graded manner. Nowadays, in the proposed curriculum of Wifaq al-Madaris al-Arabiyya Pakistan, the last book taught on Usul al-Fiqh is al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Technically, al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is a complex and very subtle book. The scholarly profundities of the researcher al-Taftazani are abundant. In this delicate era of academic stagnation, teaching and learning these technical books without assistance is extremely difficult, as is observed. An experienced and expert teacher, my brother Mawlana Muhammad Luqman (may his shadow endure), teacher of Hadith at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, after teaching al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih several times, authored al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih as a summary. Mashallah, the book is aptly named: it includes analysis of the text along with translation and explanation of the commentator's objectives in a good style, while lexical and morphological investigation of difficult words is among its additional merits. It is hoped that this scholarly effort of my brother will prove beneficial for both scholars and students. By writing al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, my brother has added to the authored works of Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala. I pray that Allah, His Glory be Exalted, grants acceptance to this commentary and to his previously published Misbah al-Hikmah Sharh Hidayah al-Hikmah. Ameen, by the station of the Master of the Messengers. The supplicant, Hamid Hasan, teacher at Dar al-Ulum Eidgah Kabirwala, 10/5/1432 AH.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This is front matter comprising two endorsements (taqriz) for the book 'Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' by Mawlana Muhammad Luqman Jalal Furi. The first endorsement is by Muhammad Ismail Arshad, who praises the author's commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih (the well-known work by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani) as comprehensive and indispensable. He notes that the author has produced annotations that are elegant and complete, leaving no need for further explanation. The second endorsement is by Mufti Hamid Hasan, who emphasizes the importance of Usul al-Fiqh in the Dars Nizami curriculum and describes the difficulty of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. He then commends the author's commentary as a carefully prepared summary that includes textual analysis, translation, and lexical research, making it accessible to both scholars and students. Both scholars pray for the book's acceptance and widespread benefit. This passage sets the context for the work that follows.

Key Terms
تقریظ (taqriz): A scholarly endorsement or commendation of a book, often written by a respected scholar and included in the front matter.
درس نظامی (Dars Nizami): The traditional curriculum used in South Asian madrasas, developed by Mulla Nizam al-Din Sihalvi, which includes a graded study of various Islamic sciences including Usul al-Fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To critique the methodology of al-Taftazani.
B) To provide a simplified summary after teaching the original text several times.
C) To translate the original text into Urdu.
D) To replace the Dars Nizami curriculum.

Key Takeaway
Scholarly endorsements affirm the value of a commentary and orient the reader to its purpose, methodology, and place within the tradition.

Reading a Taqriz: Scholarly Endorsement in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Scholarly endorsement (taqriz) for a usul al-fiqh commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of a taqriz and evaluate its arguments in the context of Hanafi usul al-fiqh scholarship.

Core Idea
A taqriz authenticates a scholarly work by tracing its necessity, method, and place in the tradition.

This taqriz for al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih illustrates how senior scholars endorse new commentaries. It highlights the difficulty of the base text and the need for proper instruction. Understanding such endorsements helps you appreciate the chains of scholarship (isnad) and the criteria for reliable works in the Hanafi curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his credentials
Who wrote the taqriz? What positions does he hold? Why does that matter for the authenticity of the endorsement?
2
Understand the stated problem
What difficulty does the taqriz attribute to al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih? What does it say about the current intellectual climate?
3
Analyse the claimed solution
What features of the new commentary are praised? How do these features address the problem?
This is an endorsement, so we evaluate its rhetorical structure.

The Explanation for Solving al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Esteemed teacher, Mawlana Mufti Hamid Hasan Sahib, may his blessings continue, head of ifta, Muhammad and his prayers be upon his noble Messenger, and teacher of hadith at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala. After praise! Among religious sciences, the science of usul al-fiqh holds a foundational position for deriving rulings, by which understanding and teaching the Quran and Sunnah becomes easy. This is why the great scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, included other advanced and instrumental sciences in the Dars Nizami curriculum and also made usul al-fiqh a part of it. Various books on usul al-fiqh are taught in stages. Nowadays, in the prescribed syllabus of Wifaq al-Madaris al-Arabiyya Pakistan, the last book taught on usul al-fiqh is al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. From a technical perspective, al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is a very intricate and exacting book. The scholarly profundities of Muhiq al-Taftazani add to its complexity. In this delicate and intellectually stagnant era, teaching and learning such technical books without assistance is extremely difficult, as is observed. My experienced and expert brother, Mawlana Muhammad Luqman Sahib, may his shadow endure, teacher of hadith at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, after teaching al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih several times, has authored al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih as an extract. MashaAllah, the book is appropriately named, in which he has not only clarified the expressions but also provided translation and explained the intentions of the commentator in a good style. Additionally, lexical and morphological investigation of difficult words is among the extra merits. It is hoped that this scholarly effort of my respected brother will prove beneficial for both scholars and students. My respected brother has added to the authored works of Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala by writing al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Prayer is that Allah, Glorious is He, bestow acceptance upon this commentary and upon the previously published Misbah al-Hikmah Sharh Hidayah al-Hikmah. Amen, by the dignity of the Chief of the Messengers. Seeking prayers, Hamid Hasan, teacher at Dar al-Ulum Eidgah Kabirwala, 10/5/1432 AH.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a taqriz (scholarly endorsement) written by Mufti Hamid Hasan for the book al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It begins with the author's credentials and then explains the importance of usul al-fiqh in the Islamic curriculum. It highlights that al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is a very difficult book due to the depth of Taftazani's scholarship, and that a commentary is needed. The writer praises the author Muhammad Luqman for his effort, noting that the commentary provides clear explanations, translations, and lexical analysis. The endorsement concludes with a prayer for the book's acceptance.

Key Terms
تقيظ (taqriz): A scholarly endorsement or recommendation of a book.
غامض (ghamid): Intricate, difficult to understand.
أدق (adq): Very exacting, requiring precision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A taqriz serves to authenticate a scholarly work and highlight its necessity within the tradition of usul al-fiqh.

The Humble Commentator: Muhammad Luqman's Preface
Author's preface explaining motivation and method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the reasons a Hanafi scholar undertakes a commentary and evaluate the significance of scholarly humility in the transmission of knowledge.

Core Idea
A commentator's humility and reliance on established sources ensure the preservation of accurate legal knowledge.

This passage is the personal preface of Muhammad Luqman, a Hanafi scholar, to his commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It reveals his initial hesitation, his reason for writing, and his method of drawing from rare and common commentaries. This lesson explores the ethical and scholarly foundations of commentary writing in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the genre
Identify that this is a preface (taqdim) setting the context for the commentary. Prefaces often state the author's purpose and method.
The preface is a standard feature in classical scholarly works.
2
Understand the author's humility
Note the author's admission of inadequacy (ضيق البضاعة) and hesitation. He compares himself to a host with no food.
Humility before undertaking a great task is considered a virtue in Islamic scholarship.
3
Identify the motivation
The author was asked by students and teachers. Despite hesitation, he saw great benefit (مصلحة عظيمة) and service to the religion.
The request from peers and the perceived benefit overcame his reluctance.
4
Note the methodology
He relied on both rare supercommentaries (الحواشي النادرة) and widely circulated commentaries (الشروح المتداولة).
This shows a comprehensive approach to verifying sources.
5
Evaluate the significance
Consider why humility and source reliance are important for the reliability of transmitted knowledge in Hanafi usul.
A commentator's integrity affects the trustworthiness of his work.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم التقديم حمد المن جعل شجرة الشريعة الغراء محكمة بالدلائل والاصول وصير اغصان الملة البيضاء مثمرة بالاحكام والفروع والصلوة على من ارسله هدى للمتقين وسيد المرسلين وبعثه شفاء للآسين ونجاة للعاصين وشرفه بخطاب وما ارسلناک الا رحمة للعالمين وعلى آله الذين اعربوا كلمتهم عن الحق الصريح وعلى اصحابه الذين انبئوا عن الدين الصبيح وبعد فيقول العبد المغترف ببحر فضل القدير المعترف بالعجز والتقصير الراجي الى الطاف الرحمن محمد لقمان لما كان كتاب التوضيح مع التلويح فذا في استباق العوالى وجوهرا فردا في انواع المعالي و مشتملا على علوم رئيسة وفوائد شريفة ومتضمنا يواقيت عظيمة وجواهر نفيسة ومذيلا بتعريفات ثمينة وتعريفات جميلة وبلغ مرتبة علية من التحقيق حتى صارت لطائف مبانيه محجوبة كالخرائد في القصور ونفائس معانيه مستورة كالفرائد في البحور وعرج على درجة رفيعة من التدقيق حتى ضاق نطاق العقول والفهوم عن ادراك ما احاطه من المنقول والمعقول فسالنی اخوانى من المعلمين واصحابى من المحصلين ان اشرحه شرحا يحل عقد الاعضال من حقائق التوضيح ويفتح عقال العويصات من دقائق التلويح ويكفى لتبيين ما فيهما من القواعد والفوائد ويكفل لتفتيح ما فيهما من المعاقد والمقاصد وانى كنت مترددا ان اضع القدم فى هذا الوادى لقلة بضاعتى وزادی و باعترافی بانی لست اهلا لذلك ولايليق لمثلى ان يسلك تلك المسالک و مثلی من يدعو الضيوف ولا طعام ثم اذا تاملت فيه بناحية أخرى تيقنت بان فى قضاء ما اقترحوا على مصلحة عظيمة ومنفعة جسيمة وتحققت بانه امر يرجع الى خدمة الدين المتين وفيه نوع اعانة لطلباء الشرع المبين فشرعت في تاليفه مستعينا بالله آخذا من الحواشي النادرة المخفية عن الانام وعن الشروح المتداولة
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Introduction. Praise be to Him who made the tree of the noble Shariah firm with proofs and principles, and made the branches of the white faith fruitful with rulings and branches. And prayers and peace be upon the one He sent as guidance for the righteous and the chief of the messengers, and sent him as a cure for the distressed and deliverance for the disobedient, and honored him with the address 'And We have not sent you except as a mercy to the worlds.' And upon his family, who expressed their word about the clear truth, and upon his companions, who were informed about the bright religion. After this, the servant who immerses in the sea of the grace of the Almighty, who admits his incapacity and shortcoming, hoping for the favors of the Most Merciful, Muhammad Luqman, says: Since the book al-Tawdih with al-Talwih is unique in surpassing the highest ranks and a singular jewel in types of excellences, containing leading sciences and noble benefits, including great rubies and precious jewels, appended with valuable definitions and beautiful clarifications, and attained a high rank of verification until the subtleties of its structures became hidden like pearls in fortresses and the precious meanings concealed like hidden pearls in seas, and ascended to a lofty degree of precision until the scope of intellects and understandings fell short of grasping what it encompassed of transmitted and rational knowledge. So my brothers among the teachers and my companions among the students asked me to explain it with an explanation that would undo the knots of difficulty from the realities of al-Tawdih, open the shackles of perplexities from the subtleties of al-Talwih, suffice for clarifying the principles and benefits found in both, and guarantee to unlock the knots and intentions in them. I was hesitant to set foot in this valley because of the paucity of my goods and provisions, and my admission that I am not worthy of that, nor is it fitting for someone like me to tread those paths. I am like one who invites guests but has no food. Then, when I reflected on it from another angle, I became certain that in fulfilling what they proposed there is great benefit and enormous advantage, and I realized that it is a matter that pertains to serving the strong religion and contains a kind of assistance for students of the clear law. So I began composing it, seeking help from Allah, taking from the rare supercommentaries hidden from people and from the widely circulated commentaries.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (al-taqdim) to the commentary al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It opens with the basmala and praise of Allah, emphasizing the strength of the Shariah. The author, Muhammad Luqman, then praises the original text al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, describing it as unparalleled in depth and precision, yet so intricate that even intellectuals struggle. He states that he was asked by colleagues and students to write a commentary that would clarify its difficulties. He initially hesitated, feeling unqualified and lacking resources, comparing himself to someone who invites guests with no food. However, realizing the great benefit and service to Islam, he began the work, relying on Allah and drawing from rare and common commentaries. This preface establishes the author's humility and the educational need for the commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author initially hesitate to write the commentary?
A) He was too busy teaching.
B) He felt he was not qualified and lacked resources.
C) He did not like the book.
D) He wanted a co-author.

Key Takeaway
A commentator's humility and reliance on authentic sources are essential for producing reliable scholarly works that serve the religion.

Author's Introduction: Purpose and Context of al-Tarwih
Author's prefatory remarks on the book's importance and his effort

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the three parts of the author's introduction, explain his initial hesitation and motivation, and appreciate the scholarly humility expressed in his apology.

Core Idea
Scholar's humility in introduction underscores the rigorous nature of Hanafi usul commentary tradition.

This passage is the opening of the commentary 'al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' by Muhammad Luqman. It is not the start of the main textual analysis, but rather a prefatory explanation that sets the stage for the entire work. Understanding this introduction helps you grasp the author's purpose, his scholarly attitude, and the collaborative spirit in which the commentary was produced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sections
Read through the Arabic and translation to locate where the introduction (التقديم), apology (الاعتذار), and acknowledgments (التشكر) begin and end. These correspond to the author's opening praise, his apology for errors, and his thanks.
The apology starts with 'الاعتذار' and the acknowledgments with 'التشكر'.
2
Analyze the author's praise of the base texts
Notice how the author describes al-Tawdih and al-Talwih as 'unique in preeminence', containing 'great rubies and precious gems'. This establishes the high value of the texts he is commenting on.
This praise is not mere flattery but sets the expectation for the commentary's depth.
3
Understand his hesitation and motivation
The author admits to feeling inadequate (scant goods) but was convinced to proceed because of the great benefit to students of knowledge. This shows that his motivation was service to the religion, not personal ambition.
He compares himself to one who 'invites guests but has no food'—a classic expression of humility.
4
Recognize the scholarly network
The author mentions his shaykh Mufti Muhammad Abdullah, who named the commentary, and his guide Sayyid Javed Hussain Shah. This indicates the commentary was produced under guidance and approval of established scholars.
The naming of a work by a shaykh was a mark of endorsement.
5
Reflect on the apology and its implications
The author acknowledges that errors are possible due to the difficulty of the texts, and he asks readers to overlook shortcomings and point out mistakes. This reflects the Hanafi tradition of scholarly openness and the recognition that only the infallible are free from error.
This apology is a standard feature in many Islamic scholarly works, emphasizing adab.

حمد المن جعل شجرة الشريعة الغراء محكمة بالدلائل والاصول وصير اغصان الملة البيضاء مثمرة بالاحكام والفروع والصلوة على من ارسله هدى للمتقين وسيد المرسلين وبعثه شفاء للآسين ونجاة للعاصين وشرفه بخطاب وما ارسلناک الا رحمة للعالمين وعلى آله الذين اعربوا كلمتهم عن الحق الصريح وعلى اصحابه الذين انبئوا عن الدين الصبيح وبعد فيقول العبد المغترف ببحر فضل القدير المعترف بالعجز والتقصير الراجي الى الطاف الرحمن محمد لقمان

الاعتذار
لا يخفى على اهل النظر ان كتاب التوضيح والتلويح من ادق الكتب التي صنفت في اصول الفقه وعباراته صعبة وجزلة وبيان مفاهيمهما كما حقه مشكل فوقوع الزلات والغلطات ممكن وان بذلت الجهد المكثف فى تصحيح التعبيرات عن المقصود مع ذلك ما ابرئ نفسي عن وقوع الخطأ في التقريرات وعن مساوقة السهو في التعبيرات لان لا يخفى على المستنيرين ان لايسع المجال للانسان سوى المعصومين ان يصيب الصواب فى كل باب من الابواب وان يتخلف عنه السهو والنسيان في كل مادة من المواد فارجو من طالبى طريق الصواب وشاربي رحيق السداد ان ينظروا اليه بعين العناية والوداد والا يركزوا نحوه بالعداوة والفساد ويعرضوا عن الاعتراض بالجدل والعناد والتمس من الافاضل ان يحددوا مواضع الاخطاء في التقرير والتعبير لكي اسددها في الطبع الثاني من التحرير
التشكر
واشکر آخرا روافدى وتلامذتى الذين اعانونى على ضبط الارقام التي قرأوها على عند القاء الدرس عليهم بدار العلوم كبير و الا وساعدوني على كتابة الوصفة وبذلوا جهدهم في تصحيح البروقات والذين عزروني في تنضيد احرف الكتب وامدونى بطبعها واشاعتها. والله تعالى المسئول منه الرضا والقبول والمامول منه العصمة عن الزلة فيما اقول عليه توكلت واليه انيب. وهو حسبى ونعم الوكيل. آمین بجاہ سید المرسلین
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction: Praise be to Allah who made the tree of the noble Sharia firmly established with proofs and principles, and made the branches of the white religion fruitful with rulings and branches. And blessings be upon the one He sent as guidance for the righteous and the master of messengers, and sent him as a cure for the sorrowful and deliverance for the disobedient, and honored him with the address 'And We have not sent you except as a mercy to the worlds.' And upon his family who expressed their word about clear truth, and upon his companions who were told about the sound religion. After this, the servant who immerses in the sea of the grace of the Almighty, who admits helplessness and deficiency, who hopes for the favors of the Most Merciful, Muhammad Luqman, says: Since the book al-Tawdih together with al-Talwih is unique in preeminence and a singular jewel in varieties of excellence, and includes major sciences and noble benefits, and contains great rubies and precious gems, and is appended with valuable definitions and beautiful clarifications, and reached a high rank of verification such that the subtleties of its meanings are hidden like pearls in fortresses and the treasures of its concepts are concealed like precious stones in seas, and ascended to a sublime degree of precision such that the scope of intellects and understandings is too narrow to grasp what it encompasses of transmitted and rational knowledge. So my brothers from among the teachers and my companions from among the students asked me to write a commentary on it that would untie the knots of difficulty from the realities of al-Tawdih and unlock the locks of perplexities from the intricacies of al-Talwih, and suffice to clarify the rules and benefits in them, and guarantee to open the ties and objectives in them. I was hesitant to set foot in this valley due to my scant goods and provision, and due to my admission that I am not worthy of that and it is not fitting for someone like me to tread those paths, and someone like me invites guests but has no food. Then when I considered it from another angle, I became certain that in fulfilling what they proposed there is a great benefit and immense advantage, and I realized that it is a matter that pertains to serving the strong religion and contains a kind of assistance for students of the clear Sharia. So I began composing it, seeking help from Allah, taking from the rare glosses hidden from people and from the widespread commentaries among the virtuous, and from the annotations and lectures recorded by the great teachers. When I completed a draft and presented it to my shaykh, he named it, my master and support, Mufti Muhammad Abdullah, 'al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' and it was approved by my beloved and guide Sayyid Javed Hussain Shah, may Allah continue their blessings. Apology: It is not hidden from those with insight that the book al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is among the most exact books composed in usul al-fiqh; its expressions are difficult and eloquent, and explaining its meanings as they deserve is problematic. So occurrence of slips and mistakes is possible. Even though I exerted concentrated effort in correcting the expressions concerning the intended meaning, I do not absolve myself of falling into error in the discussions and of the occurrence of forgetfulness in the expressions. Because it is not hidden from the enlightened that it is not possible for a person, other than the infallible, to hit the mark in every chapter and to be free from forgetfulness and oversight in every matter. So I ask from those who seek the path of correctness and drink the nectar of soundness to look at it with an eye of care and affection, and not to direct towards it hostility and corruption, and to refrain from objection with argument and stubbornness. And I request from the virtuous to identify the places of error in the discussion and expression so that I may correct them in the second printing of the draft. Acknowledgment: I also thank my students and disciples who helped me in recording the lessons that they read back to me when I lectured them at Dar al-Ulum Kabir, and who assisted me in writing the prescription [the commentary] and exerted their efforts in correcting the proofs, and who helped me in typesetting the letters of the books and assisted me in printing and distributing it. Allah is the One from whom we seek acceptance and approval, and from whom is hoped protection from slip in what I say. Upon Him I rely and to Him I turn. He is sufficient for me and the best trustee. Amen, through the status of the Master of the Messengers.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his commentary 'al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. The author, Muhammad Luqman, begins with the basmala, praise to Allah, and blessings upon the Prophet, his family, and companions—a standard opening in Islamic scholarly works. He then explains the value of the base text, al-Tawdih (by Sadr al-Shariah) and its supercommentary al-Talwih (by al-Taftazani), describing them as unique works containing deep proofs and precise definitions. He states that colleagues requested he write an explanatory commentary to clarify difficult points. Initially hesitant due to his own perceived inadequacy, he later recognized the great benefit in serving students of knowledge. He compiled the commentary using rare glosses and well-known commentaries. After preparing a draft, his shaykh, Mufti Muhammad Abdullah, named it 'al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih', and it was also approved by his guide Sayyid Javed Hussain Shah. In the apology section, he acknowledges the difficulty of the base texts and the possibility of errors despite his efforts, asking readers to overlook shortcomings and to point out mistakes for correction in a second edition. Finally, he thanks his students who helped in recording lessons, correcting proofs, and assisting in printing and distribution. This introduction exemplifies the humility and scholarly care characteristic of classical Islamic academic works.

Key Terms
التوضيح (al-Tawdih): The base text by Sadr al-Shariah on Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
التلويح (al-Talwih): The supercommentary by al-Taftazani on al-Tawdih.
الترويح (al-Tarwih): The commentary by Muhammad Luqman on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, meaning 'refreshment for solving'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author initially hesitate to write this commentary?
A) He felt the book was too easy.
B) He lacked time due to teaching.
C) He considered himself inadequate and unworthy.
D) He did not have access to the base texts.

Key Takeaway
The introduction of a Hanafi usul commentary typically includes a statement of purpose, an apology for shortcomings, and acknowledgments, reflecting the scholarly values of humility and collaboration.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Scholarly Humility in the Author's Preface
Author's preface with apology and gratitude

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of an author's preface in classical Hanafi usul works and explain the scholarly etiquette of acknowledging fallibility.

Core Idea
True scholarship combines mastery with humility—acknowledging potential error invites correction and growth.

The preface of a classical scholarly work is not mere formality; it reveals the author's scholarly character and sets the tone for the reader. In this lesson, we examine the author's apology (i'tidhar) and gratitude (tashakkur) from his commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Understanding this front matter helps us appreciate the intellectual tradition of Hanafi usul and the adab of seeking knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structural components
Break down the preface into its parts: basmala, title, apology (i'tidhar), and gratitude (tashakkur). Note what each section does.
This is a typical structure for classical scholarly front matter.
2
Understand the apology's rationale
The author states that al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih are among the most precise and difficult works on usul. He acknowledges that despite intense effort, errors are possible. Why does he emphasize this?
He is not making excuses but setting realistic expectations and inviting constructive feedback.
3
Recognize the scholarly adab
The author asks readers to look with care and affection, not enmity, and to refrain from stubborn objection. He requests identification of errors for correction in future editions. What does this teach about scholarly interaction?
This reflects the Hanafi tradition of respectful debate and continuous improvement.
4
Analyze the gratitude section
The author thanks his teachers, students, and supporters for their help in recording, proofreading, typesetting, and disseminating the work. How does this highlight the collaborative nature of scholarship?
Islamic scholarship is rarely a solitary endeavor; it involves a community of learners and benefactors.
5
Reflect on the author's final supplication
The author ends with a prayer for Allah's acceptance and protection from error. How does this frame the entire work within a spirit of tawakkul (reliance on Allah)?
This reminds us that ultimate correctness belongs to Allah alone; the scholar is merely a vessel.

Among the distinguished scholars and from the annotations and written commentaries of the great professors. 43. Because it is not hidden from the enlightened that it is not within the capacity of a human, except the infallible ones, to hit correctness in every chapter and for forgetfulness and negligence to be absent from every material. So I hope from the seekers of the path of correctness and the drinkers of the nectar of rectitude that they look at it with an eye of care and affection, and not focus on it with enmity and corruption, and refrain from objection with debate and stubbornness. Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It begins with the basmala and the title of his work. He then offers an apology (i'tidhar) acknowledging the difficulty of the source texts and the possibility of errors despite his efforts. He humbly requests readers to overlook mistakes and to point out errors for correction in future editions. Finally, he expresses gratitude (tashakkur) to his teachers, students, and supporters who assisted in the preparation and publication of the book. This is typical front matter in classical scholarly works, showing the author's humility and academic rigor.

Key Terms
التوضيح والتلويح (al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih): Two foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh texts: al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah and al-Talwih by Taftazani, which is a supercommentary on al-Tawdih.
الاعتذار (al-i'tidhar): Apology; the author excuses himself for any errors due to the difficulty of the subject.
التشكر (al-tashakkur): Gratitude; the author thanks his teachers, students, and supporters.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Preliminaries of Usul al-Fiqh: Definitions, Subject, and Need
Introducing the basic preliminaries of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the separate and composite definitions of usul al-fiqh and explain its subject matter and the rationale for its necessity.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of principles that lead to fiqh with verification — its subject is the four proofs and its need arises from infinite new incidents.

Every science begins with preliminaries, and usul al-fiqh is no exception. This passage introduces the two ways to define usul al-fiqh: by defining its parts separately (ta'rif idafi) and by defining the compound as a whole (ta'rif laqami). It then clarifies the subject matter—the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas)—and answers a common objection: if the Companions did not need this science, why did later generations? The response: humans face countless new incidents that require a systematic method for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of preliminaries
Note the six standard preliminaries the author lists (definition, subject, purpose, need, first compiler, author's circumstances). This lesson focuses on definition, subject, and need.
These are typical in Islamic sciences introductions.
2
Distinguish between ta'rif idafi and ta'rif laqami
Ta'rif idafi defines 'usul' and 'fiqh' separately. Ta'rif laqami defines the compound 'usul al-fiqh' as a whole. Understand the logical structure: 'usul' (pl. of asl) as foundation, 'fiqh' as knowledge of practical rulings from detailed proofs.
The composite definition includes the key phrase 'by which one arrives at fiqh in a verified manner'.
3
Identify the subject matter
The subject is the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) considered as sources for deriving rulings and for understanding the methodology of ijtihad.
Fiqh looks at proofs for specific rulings; usul looks at proofs for the method of derivation.
4
Evaluate the need for usul al-fiqh
The objection: Companions didn't need it. The answer: human actions are infinite; new incidents arise daily; a systematic method (principles) is required to deduce rulings for new situations after the age of direct linguistic intuition ended.
This establishes usul al-fiqh as a necessary tool for ijtihad.

مصنفین کی عادت ہے کہ وہ کتاب کو شروع کرنے سے پہلے اس فن کے متعلق کچھ مبادیات ذکر کرتے ہیں جس میں وہ کتاب تصنیف کر رہے ہوتے ہیں اور وہ مندرجہ ذیل ہیں (۱) تعریف (۲) موضوع (۳) غرض و غایت (۴) ضرورت (۵) مدون اول (۶) حالات مصنف
اس لئے اختصارا ہم بھی ان کے بارہ میں کچھ معروضات زیب قرطاس کریں گے
تعریف اصول فقہ
تعریف کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) تعریف اضافی (۲) تعریف تعمی [لعمی]
تعریف اضافی کہتے ہیں مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کی الگ الگ تعریف کرنا
تعریف لقمی کہتے ہیں مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کی اکٹھے تعریف کرنا محدود اگر مرکب اضافی ہو تو اس کی دونوں تعریفیں کی جاتی ہیں اصول فقہ بھی چونکہ مرکب اضافی (اصول مضاف اور فقہ مضاف الیہ ) ہے اس لئے اس کی بھی دونوں تعریفیں کی جائیں گی پہلے ہم تعریف اضافی کو ذکر کرتے ہیں تعریف مضاف (اصول)
اصول یہ مضاف ہے اور یہ جمع ہے اصل کی اور اصل کہتے ہیں مای بتنی علیہ غیرہ یعنی جس پر اس کے غیر کی بناء کی جائے عام ہے کہ ابتنا حسی ہو یا عقلی جیسے کہ چھت کی بناء دیواروں پر تو دیوار میں چھت کیلئے اصل ہیں اسی طرح حکم کی بناء دلیل پر تو دلیل حکم کیلئے اصل ہے پہلی ابتنا حسی کی مثال ہے اور دوسری ابتنا عقلی کی
تعریف مضاف الیہ ( الفقه )
فقہ کی تعین تعریفیں کی گئی ہیں ان میں سے مشہور تعریف مندرجہ ذیل ہے
هو العلم بالاحكام الشرعية العملية من ادلتها التفصيلية یعنی احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کو ادلہ تفصیلیہ سے جانے کا نام فقہ ہے
تعریف لقمی
العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بہا الی الفقہ علی وجہ اتحقیق یعنی اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کے جانے کا نام ہے جن سے فقہ کی طرف توصل قریب حاصل ہو تحقیق کے طور پر قواعد سے مراد ایسے قضا یا کلیہ ہیں جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں سے ایک مقدمہ واقع ہوتے ہیں یعنی اگر دلیل قیاس استثنائی سے پیش کی جائے تو اس کا ملازمہ کلیہ قضیہ کلیہ واقع ہوتا ہے اور اگر دلیل قیاس اقترانی کے ذریعہ پیش کی جائے تو شکل اول کا کبری قضیہ کلیہ بنتا ہے اس کی مزید تفصیل علامہ صدر الشریعہ نے خود کتاب میں کر دی ہے
فوائد قیود
علم بمنزل جنس کے ہے اور توصل کی قید بمنزل فصل کے ہے اس سے علوم عربیہ نکل گئے کیونکہ توصل سے مراد توصل قریب ہے یعنی بغیر واسطہ کے فقہ تک پہنچا دیں کیونکہ بہا میں باء سیبیہ ہے اور الی الفقہ سے معلوم ہورہا ہے کہ توصل فقہ تک بلا واسطہ ہو اور علوم عربیہ سے فقہ تک توصل قریب حاصل نہیں ہوتا علی وجہ اتحقیق یہ فصل ثانی ہے اس سے علم مناظرہ و جدل وغیرہ خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ ان سے مقصود خصم کو الزام دینا ہوتا ہے مسائل فقہ کی تحقیق مقصود نہیں ہوتی
موضوع اصول فقه
اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اربعہ یعنی کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اللہ اجماع اور قیاس ہیں اس حیثیت سے کہ ان سے طریق استنباط اور مراتب حجیت معلوم ہوں خلاصہ یہ کہ فقہ اور اصول فقہ میں علوم کا تو ارد ادلہ پر ہی ہوتا ہے لیکن ڈرود کی حیثیت مختلف ہے کہ فقہ کا ورو د ادلہ پر اس حیثیت سے ہوتا ہے کہ اولہ سے احکام جزئیہ عملیہ کا استخراج ہو سکے اور اصول فقہ کا ورود ادلہ پر اس حیثیت سے ہوتا ہے کہ ان ادلہ اربعہ سے استنباط مسائل اور اجتہاد مسائل کا طریقہ معلوم ہو سکے
ضرورت ایں فن
عام طور پر یہ اشکال عوام و خواص کی زباں زد ہے کہ دین کا مدار صحابہ کرام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین کی قدسیہ صفات جماعت پر ہے جبکہ ان کے دور میں ان علوم یعنی فقہ اصول فقہ اصول حدیث اصول تغییر وغیرہ کو مدون نہیں کیا گیا اور نہ ہی اس کی ضرورت کبھی گئی پھر آخر خیر القرون کے ادوار کے بعد ان کو مدون کرنے کی ضرورت کیوں پیش آئی ؟
جواب:۔ اس اشکال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ انسان کو بیہ کار اور سدی پیدا نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ اس کے ہر فعل کے ساتھ کوئی نہ کوئی حکم شرعی متعلق ہے اور افعال انسانیت غیر متناہی ہیں نئے نئے حوادثات و واقعات روز بروز معرض وجود میں آتے رہتے ہیں اور قیامت تک ان کا اضافہ ہوتا رہے گا اب ہر فعل اور جزئی کا حکم معلوم کرنا مشکل ہے اس لئے ایسے قواعد کی تدوین کی ضرورت
It is the habit of authors that before beginning a book, they mention some preliminaries related to that science in which they are writing the book, and they are as follows: (1) Definition (2) Subject (3) Purpose and Goal (4) Need (5) First Compiler (6) Conditions of the Author. Therefore, briefly, we too will write some observations about them.
Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: There are two types of definition: (1) Separate definition (ta'rif idafi) (2) Composite definition (ta'rif laqami). Separate definition means defining the mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately. Composite definition means defining mudaf and mudaf ilayh together. If the defined term is a genitive compound, then both definitions are given. Since usul al-fiqh is a genitive compound (usul as mudaf and fiqh as mudaf ilayh), therefore both its definitions will be given. First we mention the separate definition.
Definition of the Mudaf (Usul): Usul is mudaf and it is the plural of asl. Asl is defined as 'that on which something else is built' (ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh) i.e., that on which something other than itself is based, whether the foundation is sensory or intellectual. For example, the building of a roof on walls, so the walls are asl for the roof. Similarly, the building of a ruling on a proof, so the proof is asl for the ruling. The first is an example of sensory foundation, and the second of intellectual foundation.
Definition of Mudaf Ilayh (al-Fiqh): Several definitions of fiqh have been given. Among them, the famous definition is: 'Knowledge of practical legal rulings from their detailed proofs' (huwa al-'ilm bi al-ahkam al-shar'iyyah al-'amaliyyah min adillatiha al-tafṣiliyyah). That is, to know the practical legal rulings from their detailed proofs is called fiqh.
Composite Definition (Ta'rif Laqami): 'Knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh in a verified manner' (al-'ilm bi al-qawa'id allati yutawassalu biha ila al-fiqh 'ala wajh al-tahqiq). That is, usul al-fiqh is the name of knowing such principles from which a close means of access to fiqh is obtained in a verified manner. By 'principles' are meant such universal propositions which form one of the two premises of a proof. That is, if the proof is presented by way of exceptional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i), then its conjunctive universal proposition becomes a universal proposition. And if the proof is presented by way of conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani), then the major premise of the first figure becomes a universal proposition. Further details have been given by 'Allamah Sadr al-Shari'ah himself in the book.
Benefits of the Restrictions: 'Knowledge' (al-'ilm) is like the genus, and the restriction 'by which one arrives' (al-tawassul) is like the differentia. By this, the Arabic sciences (al-'ulum al-'arabiyyah) are excluded, because by 'tawassul' is meant close access, i.e., reaching fiqh without an intermediary, since the ba' in biha is sababiyyah, and 'ila al-fiqh' indicates that the access to fiqh is without intermediary. And from the Arabic sciences, a close access to fiqh is not obtained. 'In a verified manner' ('ala wajh al-tahqiq) is a second differentia. By this, the science of debate (al-munazarah) and dialectic (al-jadal) etc. are excluded, because their purpose is to compel the opponent, not to verify the issues of fiqh.
Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh: The subject matter of usul al-fiqh is the four proofs, i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas), from the perspective that from them the method of deduction and the levels of authority are known. In summary, both fiqh and usul al-fiqh are concerned with proofs, but the relationship is different: fiqh concerns proofs in the sense that from them individual practical rulings can be extracted, while usul al-fiqh concerns proofs in the sense that from these four proofs the method of deducing issues and the method of ijtihad in issues can be known.
Need for This Science: Commonly, there is an objection on the tongues of commoners and specialists that the foundation of the religion is on the holy attributes of the group of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them all), while in their era these sciences—i.e., fiqh, usul al-fiqh, usul al-hadith, usul al-tafsir, etc.—were not compiled, nor was there ever a need for them. Then why did the need arise to compile them after the era of the best of generations?
Answer: The answer to this objection is that man was not created worthless and aimless; rather, every action of his is associated with some legal ruling, and human actions are infinite. New events and occurrences continue to come into existence day by day, and they will increase until the Day of Judgment. Now, it is difficult to know the ruling of every action and particular incident. Therefore, there is a need to compile such principles.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is the introductory section (mabadiyat) of a sharh (commentary) on usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining the common practice of scholars to mention preliminaries before their work. He then proceeds to define 'usul al-fiqh' according to two methods: the separate definition (ta'rif idafi) and the composite definition (ta'rif laqami). In the separate definition, he defines 'usul' (pl. of asl) as that on which something else is built, giving examples from both sensory (roof on walls) and intellectual (ruling on proof) foundations. For 'fiqh', he gives the well-known definition: knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from their detailed proofs. The composite definition presents usul al-fiqh as the science of principles that enable one to reach fiqh with certainty (tahqiq). He then explains the function of these principles as premises in logical syllogisms. Next, he analyzes the restrictions in the definition: 'knowledge' as genus, 'by which one arrives' as differentia excluding linguistic sciences, and 'in a verified manner' excluding dialectic and debate. The subject matter of usul al-fiqh is identified as the four primary proofs (Quran, Sunnah, consensus, analogy) viewed as sources for deriving rulings and establishing the methodology of ijtihad. Finally, the author addresses the common objection about the need for this science, arguing that human actions are unlimited and new incidents constantly arise, requiring a systematic method to derive rulings—a method that was not needed in the time of the Companions because they possessed direct linguistic and contextual understanding, but later generations required codified principles.

Key Terms
تعریف اضافی (ta'rif idafi): A definition that explains each part of a compound term separately; here, defining 'usul' and 'fiqh' independently.
تعریف لقمی (ta'rif laqami): A definition that explains the compound term as a whole, without separating its parts; here, usul al-fiqh as 'knowledge of the principles that lead to fiqh with verification'.
اصل (asl): That on which something else is built; a foundation, whether sensory (like walls for a roof) or intellectual (like a proof for a ruling).
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from their detailed proofs (al-'ilm bi al-ahkam al-shar'iyyah al-'amaliyyah min adillatiha al-tafṣiliyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the subject matter of usul al-fiqh?
A) The detailed rulings of fiqh (furū')
B) The four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) from the perspective of method of deduction and levels of authority

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh provides the methodological principles to derive practical Shar'i rulings from the four proofs, ensuring systematic and verifiable ijtihad.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The First Codifiers of Usul al-Fiqh: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Shafi'i
Historical overview of early usul codification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the historical development of Usul al-Fiqh as a distinct discipline, identify the contributions of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Shafi'i, and explain why Imam Shafi'i's Risalah is considered the first formal work on Usul al-Fiqh.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa laid the foundation of Usul al-Fiqh, but Imam Shafi'i wrote the first systematic book.

This passage takes us back to the origins of Usul al-Fiqh as a codified discipline. While early mujtahids like Imam Abu Hanifa certainly operated with implicit principles, it was his students, the Sahibayn, who may have written lost works, and it was Imam Shafi'i who produced the first surviving comprehensive treatise: the Risalah. Understanding this history helps us appreciate the evolution of Hanafi usul methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key claims
First, that Imam Abu Hanifa is the first codifier of fiqh, but he did not write a book on usul. Second, that Imam Shafi'i wrote the first known book on usul, the Risalah.
Note the contrast: fiqh vs. usul codification.
2
Examine the evidence for Hanafi usul works
The passage mentions that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) may have written some books on usul, but they are lost. This indicates early Hanafi interest in usul.
3
Analyze the contents of the Risalah
The Risalah covered ten key topics: Quran and Sunnah, their status, abrogation, hadith causes, khabar al-wahid, qiyas, ijtihad, ijma, istihsan, and ikhtilaf. This set the agenda for later usul works.
These topics became standard in later usul manuals.
4
Understand the historical significance
The Risalah marks the formal beginning of Usul al-Fiqh as an independent science. It provided a systematic methodology that later Hanafi scholars engaged with.

مدون اول
یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ تمام مجتہدین نے اپنے اپنے طرز اجتہاد کے مطابق مسائل کا استنباط کیا اور یہ بات بھی ظاہر ہے کہ مجتہد کیلئے اصول وضوابط کے بغیر مسائل اجتہادیہ کو بیان کرنا ممکن نہیں اور یہ بات بھی متفق علیہ ہے کہ علم فقہ کے مدون اول سراج الائمہ امام ابو حنیفہ ہیں تو یقینا آپ نے تدوین فقہ کے وقت اصول فقہ کی بھی بنیاد ڈالی ہوگی لیکن اس فن مین آپ سے کوئی کتاب تحریر نہ ہوسکی البتہ علامہ خضری علیہ الرحمہ نے لکھا ہے کہ صاحبین نے اصول فقہ پر کچھ کتب تصنیف کی تھیں مگر اس وقت ان کا صحیح سراغ لگا نا بہت مشکل ہے
اصول فقہ میں سب سے پہلی تصنیف جو کتابی شکل میں آئی امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کا وہ رسالہ ہے جس کو امام شافعی نے کتاب الام کا مقدمہ بنایا ہے جس میں آپ نے (۱) قرآن وسنت کا بیان (۲) قرآن و سنت کا مقام (۳) ناسخ و منسوخ (۴) علل احادیث (۵) خبر واحد (8) قیاس (۷) اجتہاد (۸) اجماع (۹) استحسان (۱۰) اختلاف سے بحث کی ہے
First Codifier
It is accepted that all mujtahids derived issues according to their own style of ijtihad. It is also evident that for a mujtahid it is impossible to explain ijtihadi issues without principles and rules. And it is agreed upon that the first codifier of the science of fiqh is Siraj al-A'immah Imam Abu Hanifa. So certainly he must have laid the foundation of Usul al-Fiqh at the time of codifying fiqh. However, he could not write a book on this science. But 'Allamah Khudari - may Allah have mercy on him - wrote that the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) composed some books on Usul al-Fiqh, but at present it is very difficult to trace them.
The first work on Usul al-Fiqh that came in book form is the Risalah of Imam Shafi'i - may Allah have mercy on him - which Imam Shafi'i made the introduction to his book al-Umm. In it, he discussed: (1) The statement of Quran and Sunnah, (2) The status of Quran and Sunnah, (3) Abrogating and abrogated, (4) Causes of hadith, (5) Khabar al-Wahid (single narration), (6) Qiyas (analogy), (7) Ijtihad, (8) Ijma (consensus), (9) Istihsan (juristic preference), (10) Ikhtilaf (disagreement).
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage discusses the historical development of Usul al-Fiqh. It states that although Imam Abu Hanifa is recognized as the first codifier of fiqh in a systematic way, he did not author a separate book on Usul al-Fiqh. However, his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) allegedly wrote some works on the subject, now lost. The first known complete book on Usul al-Fiqh is Imam Shafi'i's Risalah, which he wrote as a preface to his major work al-Umm. The Risalah covered fundamental topics like Quran and Sunnah, abrogation, hadith criticism, consensus, analogy, ijtihad, istihsan, and disagreement. This marks the beginning of the formal discipline of Usul al-Fiqh.

Key Terms
رسالہ (Risalah): The first written work on Usul al-Fiqh by Imam Shafi'i
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who wrote the first known book on Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Shafi'i
C) Abu Yusuf
D) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Takeaway
The first systematic book on Usul al-Fiqh is Imam Shafi'i's Risalah, despite Imam Abu Hanifa being the first to systematize fiqh itself.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Historical Development of Usul al-Fiqh
Traces why usul al-fiqh was codified later and its early works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the historical development of usul al-Fiqh, explain why it was not codified in the early period, and identify key early works and their authors.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh was not needed by the Companions due to their innate juristic intuition; it was later codified to guide later scholars without that direct experience.

This passage explains why the formal science of usul al-Fiqh emerged later in Islamic history, not during the time of the Companions. It then provides a chronological overview of the earliest works, from the Risala of Imam al-Shafi'i to the 7th century writings, highlighting the evolution of style from theological to logical. Understanding this history helps contextualize the Hanafi approach to usul.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Identify why early Muslims did not need usul al-Fiqh: the Companions had natural juristic intuition (jila qalbi) and proximity to revelation; the Successors had few new incidents. Later generations lacked these qualities, so they needed systematic principles.
The text uses the analogy of 'light of prophethood' enabling direct understanding.
2
Recognize the solution
The absence of early codification does not mean ignorance; rather, the principles were known but not yet compiled into a formal discipline.
The author calls this a 'subtle point' (daqiq).
3
Note the first codifier
Imam Abu Hanifa is considered the first codifier of fiqh, implying he laid the foundation of usul, but no written work from him survives. His disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) reportedly wrote books, now lost.
This shows the primacy of Hanafi usul even without extant texts.
4
Identify the first formal book
Imam al-Shafi'i's al-Risala (late 2nd century) is the first known book on usul, covering ten key topics: Quran and Sunnah, abrogation, khabar wahid, qiyas, ijtihad, ijma, istihsan, and ikhtilaf.
The list in the text numbers 10, but one item is missing due to scribal error (8 appears twice).
5
Follow the chronological development
The passage then surveys centuries: 3rd: Maturidi's two works; 4th: al-Dhakhira and al-Usul (al-Jassas); 5th: mutakallimun style emphasizing refutation of innovators; 6th: logical argumentation (e.g., al-Mahsul); 7th: combining juristic and theological styles.
This pattern reflects broader Islamic intellectual history.

مدون اول
یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ تمام مجتہدین نے اپنے اپنے طرز اجتہاد کے مطابق مسائل کا استنباط کیا اور یہ بات بھی ظاہر ہے کہ مجتہد کیلئے اصول وضوابط کے بغیر مسائل اجتہادیہ کو بیان کرنا ممکن نہیں اور یہ بات بھی متفق علیہ ہے کہ علم فقہ کے مدون اول سراج الائمہ امام ابو حنیفہ ہیں تو یقینا آپ نے تدوین فقہ کے وقت اصول فقہ کی بھی بنیاد ڈالی ہوگی لیکن اس فن مین آپ سے کوئی کتاب تحریر نہ ہوسکی البتہ علامہ خضری علیہ الرحمہ نے لکھا ہے کہ صاحبین نے اصول فقہ پر کچھ کتب تصنیف کی تھیں مگر اس وقت ان کا صحیح سراغ لگا نا بہت مشکل ہے
اصول فقہ میں سب سے پہلی تصنیف جو کتابی شکل میں آئی امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کا وہ رسالہ ہے جس کو امام شافعی نے کتاب الام کا مقدمہ بنایا ہے جس میں آپ نے (۱) قرآن وسنت کا بیان (۲) قرآن و سنت کا مقام (۳) ناسخ و منسوخ (۴) علل احادیث (۵) خبر واحد (8) قیاس (۷) اجتہاد (۸) اجماع (۹) استحسان (۱۰) اختلاف سے بحث کی ہے
یه کوشش دوسری صدی ہجری کے آخر میں ہوئی
اصول فقہ اور تیسری صدی
تیسری صدی کے شروع میں شیخ ابو منصور ماتریدی علیہ الرحمہ نے اصول فقہ میں دو کتابیں تصنیف کیں (۱) کتاب الجدل (۲) ماخذ الشرع یہ دونوں کتابیں غایت احکام اور اتقان میں بے مثل ہیں اور ان میں اصول و فروع کو کثرت سے ذکر کیا گیا ہے
اصول فقہ اور چوتھی صدی
اس صدی میں اصول فقہ کی متعدد کتابیں معرض وجود میں آئیں اور اس دور کی عمدہ ترین کتابیں دو ہیں (۱) کتاب الذخیرہ جو شیخ احمد بن برہان فارسی کی تالیف ہے (۲) کتاب الاصول جو امام ابو بکر جصاص احمد بن علی حنفی کی تصنیف ہے۔
اصول فقہ اور پانچویں صدی
اس صدی میں علماء نے اس فن پر بہت زیادہ کام کیا جس کے نتیجہ میں تقریبا دس عمدہ کتابیں وجود میں آئیں مثلاً (۱) الانوار (۲) تقویم الادلہ (۳) کفایه (۴) تبصره (۵) تذكرة العالم والطريق السالم (۶) اللہ (۷) کتاب البرہان (۸) اصول فخر اسلام ( کشف) جس کے ضوابط کو علامہ صدر الشریعہ نے تنقیح میں ذکر کیا ہے لیکن اس دور میں اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں متکلمانہ طرز نمایاں ہے یعنی اکثر کتابوں کی تصنیف متکلمین کے طرز پر کی گئی ہے جن میں اہل بدعت پر الزام طرزنمایاں اور ان پر سخت تنقید کی گئی ہے
اصول فقہ اور چھٹی صدی
چھٹی صدی میں جو کہتا ہیں اصول فقہ میں تصنیف کی گئیں ان میں استدلال اور احتجاج کی طرف زیادہ میلان ہے یعنی دلائل کو منطقی انداز میں پیش کیا گیا ہے اور اس دور کی مشہور کتا ہیں یہ ہیں (۱) الاصول جو علامہ قاضی القضاة حنفی کی تصنیف ہے (۲) المغنی (۳) محصول جو علامہ فخر الدین رازی کی تصنیف ہے اور تنقیح میں اس کا خلاصہ بھی موجود ہے
اصول فقہ اور ساتویں صدی
اس دور میں اصول فقہ پر کئی کتب تصنیف کی گئیں اور ان میں سے اکثر کتابوں میں قواعد پر مسائل کی تفریح کی طرف زیادہ توجہ دیہ گئی ہے اور کچھ کتابوں میں فقیہانہ اور متکلمانہ دونوں طرزوں کو جمع کیا گیا ہے اس کے بعد تیرہویں صدی تک فن
Through which the method of deriving rulings from Islamic proofs could be known. The remaining objection is: why was this need not felt in the era of the noble Companions and the great Successors? The solution to this knot is that the Companions, due to their sharpness of mind and the blessing of Prophetic company, were independent of this art and of learning such rules. That is, due to witnessing the light of prophethood, an aptitude had developed in their hearts that they would reach the goal without means and without specifying paths. That is, without needing these rules, they had the ability and capacity to know the rulings of particulars. Similarly, the Successors were close to the time of the Prophet, their beliefs were correct, events and incidents were few, and they had the power to refer to trustworthy people. Therefore, they too were independent of this art. Since this characteristic was not possessed by later people, they cannot be compared to these select personalities. So understand, for it is subtle. Further, you can also express it this way: Although the Companions and Successors knew these principles and rules, in their era this science, i.e., usul al-fiqh, had not taken the form of an industry and art like other sciences. Therefore, just as the codification of other sciences did not occur in that era, similarly the codification of usul al-fiqh did not come into being. And since after the era of the Companions, every science took the form of an art and industry, the codification of this art was also done in the form of an industry. First codifier: It is accepted that all mujtahids derived matters according to their own style of ijtihad, and it is also apparent that it is not possible for a mujtahid to express ijtihadi matters without principles and rules. It is also agreed upon that the first codifier of the science of fiqh is Siraj al-A'imma Imam Abu Hanifa. So certainly he must have laid the foundation of usul al-fiqh at the time of codifying fiqh. However, no book on this art could be written by him. But Allama Khadri (may Allah have mercy on him) wrote that the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) had composed some books on usul al-fiqh, but it is very difficult to trace them correctly now. The first composition on usul al-fiqh that came in book form is the Risala of Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), which Imam Shafi'i made the introduction to Kitab al-Umm. In it he discussed: (1) statement of Quran and Sunnah, (2) status of Quran and Sunnah, (3) abrogating and abrogated, (4) causes of hadiths, (5) khabar wahid, (8) qiyas, (7) ijtihad, (8) ijma, (9) istihsan, (10) ikhtilaf. This effort occurred at the end of the second century Hijri. Usul al-fiqh and the third century: At the beginning of the third century, Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah have mercy on him) composed two books on usul al-fiqh: (1) Kitab al-Jadal, (2) Makhidh al-Shar. Both these books are unparalleled in extreme excellence and perfection, and in them principles and branches are mentioned abundantly. Usul al-fiqh and the fourth century: In this century, numerous books on usul al-fiqh came into existence, and the best books of this period are two: (1) Kitab al-Dhakhira by Shaykh Ahmad bin Burhan al-Farsi, (2) Kitab al-Usul by Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas Ahmad bin Ali al-Hanafi. Usul al-fiqh and the fifth century: In this century, scholars worked extensively on this art, resulting in almost ten excellent books, e.g., (1) al-Anwar, (2) Taqwim al-Adilla, (3) Kifaya, (4) Tabira, (5) Tadhkirat al-Alam wa al-Tariq al-Salim, (6) Allah [unclear], (7) Kitab al-Burhan, (8) Usul Fakhr al-Islam (Kashf), whose rules Allama Sadr al-Sharia mentioned in al-Tanqih. But in this era, the mutakallimun style was prominent in books of usul al-fiqh, i.e., most books were composed in the style of the mutakallimin, in which accusing the people of innovation was prominent and severe criticism was made against them. Usul al-fiqh and the sixth century: In the sixth century, the books composed on usul al-fiqh had a greater inclination towards argumentation and proof, i.e., proofs were presented in a logical manner. The famous books of this period are: (1) al-Usul by Allama Qadi al-Qudat al-Hanafi, (2) al-Mughni, (3) al-Mahsul by Allama Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, and its summary is also present in al-Tanqih. Usul al-fiqh and the seventh century: In this era, several books were composed on usul al-fiqh, and most of them gave more attention to deriving branches from rules, and some books combined both the juristic and mutakallimun styles. After that, until the thirteenth century, the art...
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a historical account of the development of usul al-fiqh, explaining why it was not formally codified during the time of the Companions and Successors and tracing its evolution through the centuries. The author begins by addressing an objection: if usul al-fiqh is so essential, why did the early generations not need it? The answer is that the Companions possessed a natural juristic intuition (jila qalbi) and direct exposure to the Prophet's guidance, which made them independent of formal rules. Similarly, the Successors had proximity to the prophetic era, sound beliefs, and few novel incidents. Later generations, lacking these qualities, required systematic principles. The author further notes that although the early scholars knew the principles, they had not yet been compiled into a distinct discipline. The first codifier of fiqh, Imam Abu Hanifa, likely laid the foundation for usul, but no written work from him survives; his disciples reportedly wrote some books that are now lost. The first formal book on usul al-fiqh was Imam Shafi'i's al-Risala, which covered key topics like Quran and Sunnah, abrogation, khabar wahid, qiyas, ijtihad, ijma, istihsan, and ikhtilaf. This effort occurred at the end of the 2nd century Hijri. The passage then surveys the growth of usul al-fiqh in subsequent centuries: In the 3rd century, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi wrote two works; in the 4th century, al-Dhakhira by al-Farsi and al-Usul by al-Jassas; in the 5th century, numerous books appeared with a mutakallimun (theological) style emphasizing refutation of innovators; in the 6th century, works focused on logical argumentation (e.g., al-Mahsul by al-Razi); and in the 7th century, books combined fiqh-oriented and theological approaches. The passage concludes by noting that this trend continued until the 13th century. The text provides a historical overview rather than specific rulings, serving as an introductory backdrop for the study of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): The discipline that provides the method for deriving Islamic legal rulings from the Shar'i proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first known book specifically written on usul al-fiqh?
A) Al-Usul by al-Jassas
B) Al-Risala by Imam al-Shafi'i
C) Al-Mahsul by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi
D) Al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Shaybani

Key Takeaway
The formal discipline of usul al-fiqh emerged after the early generations due to the need for systematic rules; its development reflects a shift from innate intuition to codified methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Six-Book Lineage: Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih
Introduces the book's background and constituent works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the compilation history of Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih and identify the three summarized works that form their foundation.

Core Idea
Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih are not single books but a six-work chain summarising and commenting on earlier usul texts.

This lesson introduces the textual lineage behind the commentary tradition you will study. Understanding how Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih build on one another is essential for navigating their arguments. We will map the six books and their authors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main works in the chain
List the three core works: Kashf, Mahsul, al-Mukhtasar fi al-Usul. Then Tanqih, Tawdih, Talwih. That's six distinct books.
Note that Kashf is also known as Usul al-Bazdawi.
2
Understand the trend of summarization
Recognise that the passage describes a historical trend: earlier detailed works were abridged to aid memorisation. Tanqih is one such abridgment.
Other examples given include al-Hasami and al-Manar.
3
Trace the authorial lineage
Sadr al-Shariah wrote Tanqih (summary) and then its commentary Tawdih. Taftazani later wrote Talwih as a super-commentary on Tawdih.
This creates a layered commentary: original → summary → commentary → super-commentary.
4
Recognise the six-book compilation
The book you are studying (Al-Tarwih) is a gloss on Talwih, which itself comments on Tawdih, which comments on Tanqih, which summarises three earlier works. So it is a compilation of six books.
This is important for knowing which author's argument you are reading at any point.

الترویح لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيعِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ اصول فقہ پر تصنیفات کا سلسلہ جاری رہا لیکن ان ادوار میں اکثر پہلے والی مفصل کتب کا اختصار کیا گیا ہے اور اس پر توجہ دی گئی ہے کہ اصول فقہ کے مسائل کو کم از کم الفاظ میں سمیٹ دیا جائے تاکہ طلباء کیلئے یاد کرنا آسان ہو چنانچہ حسامی المنار تنقیح وغیرہ کو دیکھنے سے یہ بات واضح ہو جاتی ہے پھر انہی ادوار میں بعض لوگوں نے ان مختصر کتابوں کی تشریح بھی کی ہے مثلا نور الانوار توضیح تلویح و غیره تعارف کتاب و مصنفین یہ بظاہر دو کتا[؟] نہیں معلوم ہوتی ہیں در حقیقت یہ کئی کتابوں کا مجموعہ ہے علامہ صدرالشریعہ نے تین کتابوں کے خلاصہ کو تنقیح میں جمع کیا اور وہ تین کتب یہ ہیں (۱) کشف جو اصول بزدوی کے ساتھ معروف ہے (۲) محصول (۳) المختصر فی الاصول پھر علامہ صدر الشریعہ نے تنقیح کی شرح توضیح کے نام سے لکھی پھر توضیح کی شرح علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمہ نے کی جو کہ تلویح کے نام سے مشہور ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ یہ دراصل چھ کتابوں کا مجموعہ ہے اب ہم ہر ایک مصنف کے حالات کو مختصر اذکر کرتے ہیں
Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The series of writings on usul al-fiqh continued, but in these periods, most previous detailed books were abridged, and attention was given to summarizing the issues of usul al-fiqh in minimal words so that students could easily memorize. Thus, looking at al-Hasami, al-Manar, Tanqih, etc., this becomes clear. Then in these same periods, some people also explained these abridged books, for example, Nur al-Anwar, Tawdih, Talwih, etc. Introduction to the book and authors: Apparently, these two books are not known; in reality, it is a collection of several books. Allamah Sadr al-Shariah collected summaries of three books in Tanqih, and those three books are: (1) Kashf, which is known alongside Usul al-Bazdawi, (2) Mahsul, (3) al-Mukhtasar fi al-Usul. Then Allamah Sadr al-Shariah wrote a commentary on Tanqih named Tawdih. Then Allamah Taftazani (may Allah have mercy on him) wrote a commentary on Tawdih, which is famous as Talwih. The summary is that this is actually a collection of six books. Now we will briefly mention the circumstances of each author.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a front matter introducing the book and its compilation history. It explains that this work is not a single book but a compilation of six works: three original summaries (Kashf, Mahsul, al-Mukhtasar) collected into Tanqih by Sadr al-Shariah, then his commentary Tawdih, and then Taftazani's super-commentary Talwih. The passage also notes the trend of abridging earlier detailed usul works for easier memorization.

Key Terms
تنقیح (Tanqih): The book that summarizes three earlier works on usul al-fiqh.
توضیح (Tawdih): Commentary on Tanqih by Sadr al-Shariah.
تلویح (Talwih): Super-commentary on Tawdih by Taftazani.
کشف (Kashf): One of the three summarized books, also known as Usul al-Bazdawi.
محصول (Mahsul): One of the three summarized books, by Imam al-Razi.
المختصر فی الاصول (al-Mukhtasar fi al-Usul): One of the three summarized books, a concise work on usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many original books were summarized in Tanqih?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Six

Key Takeaway
Tanqih condenses three earlier usul works, and the commentary tradition (Tawdih, Talwih) builds on it to form a six-book resource for Hanafi usul.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Khutbah of Talwih: Praise and Methodology
Opening khutbah with praise and methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a Hanafi usul khutbah and explain the dual meaning of 'usul' in Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
Sharia's principles are rooted like a tree; its branches are raised through divine speech.

This passage is the opening khutbah of Talwih, where Allama Taftazani praises Allah and sets out the analytical framework for his commentary. Understanding the structure of such a khutbah is essential for appreciating the methodology of Hanafi usul works, as it reveals the author's sources, intentions, and interpretive approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure
Recognize that the khutbah begins with praise (hamd) after the basmalah. Note the three reasons Taftazani gives for this: following the Qur'an, hadith, and the salaf.
This triple justification shows the author's commitment to primary sources.
2
Analyze the tree metaphor
The author describes Sharia as a tree with firm roots (principles) and lofty branches (rulings). Understand that 'usul' (principles) are the foundation, and 'furu' (branches) are derived rulings.
This metaphor recurs in usul works to emphasize the dependency of furu on usul.
3
List the five matters of analysis
The Urdu commentary lists five matters that will be explained: intent of the Lawgiver, lexical analysis, analysis of intended meaning, metaphors, and research of Allama Khosrow.
These five form the author's methodology for interpreting the text of Tawdih.
4
Define 'usul'
Taftazani notes that 'usul' (plural of 'asl') can mean either general proofs (dala'il kulliyyah) or beliefs (aqa'id). Recognize that in this context, it refers primarily to the principles of Sharia.
This ambiguity is resolved by context: here it is usul al-fiqh, not usul al-din.
