Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Why Usul al-Fiqh? Taftazani's Four Reasons
Explanation of reasons for choosing usul al-fiqh as the subject of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Taftazani's four reasons for selecting usul al-fiqh and explain how each demonstrates the superiority of the discipline.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is the noblest science because it combines reason and revelation, enables ijtihad, and strengthens Sharia.

In the passage, Allamah Taftazani provides a justification for choosing usul al-fiqh as his subject. These reasons highlight the unique position of this discipline in Islamic scholarship as the foundation for ijtihad and truth.

Guided Path
1
Locate the 'Illat Ta'yin al-Fann' section
Find the part after 'علت تعیین فن' where the commentator expands on the reasons.
This follows the tamhidi muqaddimah.
2
Extract the first reason
Usul combines rational and transmitted matters (jami' li al-ma'qulat wa al-manqulat).
It encompasses Quran, hadith, ijma', qiyas.
3
Extract the second reason
It provides knowledge of non-derived issues (masa'il ghayr mustanbitah), enabling ijtihad.
Capacitates for deriving new rulings.
4
Extract the third reason
It is the most excellent science for strengthening Sharia rulings.
Afdal min ghayrihi.
5
Extract the fourth reason
It is a dignified science that serves as a refuge for intellects in manifesting truth.
Sharif, malja' al-'uqul.

:علم: اس کے دو معانی آتے ہیں (۱) جھنڈا یعنی جس طرح راستہ معلوم کرنے کے لئے جھنڈے کو علامت بنایا جاتا ہے اسی طرح دین کی ہدایت کے لئے مصنف علامت ہیں (۲) پہاڑ یعنی جس طرح راستہ معلوم کرنے کے لئے پہاڑوں کو بطور نشانی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح مصنف ہدایت کے لئے نشانی ہیں۔ عالم بمعنی جہاں ۔ درایت بمعنی سمجھ بوجھ ۔ معدل سیدھا کرنے والا ۔ منقح : صاف ستھرا کرنے والا ۔ اغصان غصن کی جمع بمعنی شہنی۔ مبسوط : بڑی کتاب۔ مستصفی: خلاصہ، نچوڑ۔ مدید لمی۔ وجيز مختصر ارکان : جمع ہے رکن کی۔ واف: صفت بعد صفت ہے یعنی پوری ہونے والی ہے کوئی چیز رہ نہیں گئی۔ وسیط درمیانی مبانی جمع ہے منی کی بمعنی بنیاد۔ سلک یسلک سلو کا چلنا۔ منهاجا : راستہ۔ بديعا : یعنی عجیب وغریب۔ اسرار : سر کی جمع ہے بمعنی راز ۔ :استولی باب استمعال سے بمعنی چڑھ جاتا۔ الامد : بمعنی غایت۔ الاقصى : انتہاء۔ منار: پرانے زمانہ میں راستہ کی تعین کے لئے ستون بناتے تھے ان پر رات کو آگ جلاتے تھے تا کہ کوئی راستہ نہ بھول جائے اب مطلق ستون کے معنی میں ہے۔ مسبتها : باب نصر بمعنی چھوٹا۔ رتق پردہ۔ افکار : فکر کی جمع ۔ فتق بمعنی فتح کھولنا۔ آذان اذن کی جمع بمعنی کان۔
تمہیدی مقدمہ :۔ عام طور پر مصنفین کی عادت ہے کہ وہ کتاب کے شروع میں مندرجہ ذیل امور بیان کرتے ہیں (۱) علت تعیین فن یعنی یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ کتاب لکھنے کے لئے اس فن کو کیوں منتخب کیا (۲) وجہ تالیف یعنی کتاب لکھنے کی غرض بیان کرتے ہیں (۳) کیفیت مصنف یعنی اپنی کتاب کی صفات بیان کرتے ہیں کہ میری یہ کتاب کس طرز پر لکھی گئی ہے (۴) اور اگر مصنف شاریخ ہو تو مذکورہ امور کے علاوہ وہ علت تعیین کتاب و متن بھی ذکر کرتا ہے یعنی میں نے شرح لکھنے کے لئے اس متن کو منتخب کیوں کیا۔
اغراض :۔ اس عبارت کے تین حصے ہیں اب ہم ہر حصہ کی غرض بیان کرینگے اور اس کے ساتھ ساتھ ہر حصہ کے متعلق کچھ سوال و جواب بھی ذکر کرینگے۔
علت تعمیین فن
قولہ وبعد : غرض شاریخ اس عبارت میں علامہ تفتازانی نے وجہ تعیین فن کو بیان فرمایا ہے کہ کتاب کو لکھنے کے لئے میں نے اس فن کو کئی وجوہ سے متعین کیا (۱) یہ علم معقولات اور منقولات کو جامع ہے کہ قرآن وحدیث منقول کے قبیل سے ہیں اور اجماع اور قیاس معقول کے قبیل سے ہیں اسی طرح بعض چیزیں دلائل عقلیہ سے معلوم ہوتی ہیں مثلا کتاب اللہ کا حجت ہونا اور بعض چیزوں کا علم دلائل نقلیہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے جیسے اکثر احکام (۲) اس علم سے مسائل غیر مستنبطہ کا علم حاصل ہوتا ہے گویا کہ اس علم سے اجتہاد کی استعداد پیدا ہوتی ہے (۳) احکام شریعت کو مضبوط کرنے کے لئے جن علوم کو قبولیت حاصل ہے ان سب سے یہ علم افضل ہے (۴) اظہار حق کے لئے جن علوم کو عقلوں کی پناہ گاہ ہونے کا شرف حاصل ہے ان میں سے یہ علم باعزت ہے اس لئے میں نے کتاب لکھنے کے لئے اس فن کو منتخب کیا۔
عطف الخبر على الانشاء
سوال:۔ و بعد میں واؤ عاطفہ ہے اور مابعد کا جملہ کے ماقبل یعنی الحمد و الصلوۃ پر عطف ہے اور یہ عطف درست نہیں کیونکہ وبعد کا مابعد جملہ خبریہ ہے اور الحمد والصلوۃ یہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے تو لازم آئے گا " عطف الخبر علی الانشاء “ اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۱):۔ جس طرح واؤ کا مابعد جملہ خبریہ ہے اسی طرح واؤ کا ماقبل بھی جملہ خبریہ ہے کیونکہ الحمدللہ میں اللہ کے حمد کے مستحق ہونے کی خبر دی گئی ہے اور والصلوۃ میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مستحق صلوۃ و سلام ہو نے کی خبر دی گئی ہے تو یہ عطف الخبر علی الخبر “ ہے۔ فلا اعتراض ۔ جواب (۲) : ۔ یہ عطف القصہ علی القصہ کے قبیل سے ہے یعنی جملہ کا عطف جملہ پر نہیں بلکہ واؤ کے بعد کے مضمون کا (۲):۔ القصہ ماقبل کے مضمون پر عطف ہے۔ جواب : یہ سوال تب وارد ہوتا جب واو عاطفہ ہو حالانکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ واؤ عوضیہ ہے اما شرطیہ کے عوض میں اس کو ذکر
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon the master of the messengers. Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih slaughters every issue, i.e. dominates every issue. 71: 'Alam: It has two meanings (1) a flag: just as a flag is made a sign to find the way, likewise the author is a sign for guidance in religion (2) a mountain: just as mountains are used as landmarks to find the way, likewise the author is a sign for guidance. 'Alim meaning world. Dirayat meaning understanding. Mu'addil meaning straightener. Munqih: cleanser. Aghsan is plural of ghusn meaning branch. Mabsut: large book. Mustasfa: summary, essence. Madid: long. Wajiz: brief. Arkan: plural of rukn. Waf: adjective after adjective meaning complete, nothing left. Wasit: intermediate. Mabani is plural of mabna meaning foundation. Salaka yasluku sulukan: to walk. Minhajan: path. Badi'an: wondrous. Asrar: plural of sirr meaning secret. Istawla: from bab isti'fal meaning to ascend. Al-Amad: meaning limit. Al-Aqsa: utmost. Manar: in ancient times they built pillars to determine the road and lit fire on them at night so that no one would forget the road; now it is used in the absolute sense of pillar. Masabtaha: from bab nasr meaning small. Ratq: veil. Afkar: plural of fikr. Fatq: meaning opening. Adhan: plural of udhun meaning ear. Preliminary Introduction: Generally, authors are accustomed to stating the following matters at the beginning of their book: (1) the reason for specifying the subject, i.e. they explain why this subject was chosen for the book; (2) the purpose of authorship, i.e. they state the goal of writing the book; (3) the quality of the book, i.e. they describe the characteristics of their book and its style; (4) and if the author is a commentator, in addition to the above matters, he also mentions the reason for choosing the book and the text, i.e. why he selected this particular text for commentary. Objectives: This passage has three parts. Now we will state the purpose of each part, and along with that we will also mention some questions and answers related to each part. Reason for specifying the subject: His saying 'Wa ba'd': The purpose of the commentator in this phrase, Allamah Taftazani, has explained the reason for specifying the subject, that he selected this subject for writing the book for several reasons: (1) This science encompasses rational and transmitted matters; Quran and hadith are from the transmitted category, and ijma' and qiyas are from the rational category. Similarly, some things are known by rational proofs, e.g. the authority of the Book of Allah, and some things are known by transmitted proofs, e.g. most rulings. (2) Through this science, knowledge of non-derived issues is obtained, i.e. this science develops the capacity for ijtihad. (3) Among the sciences accepted for strengthening the rulings of Sharia, this science is the most excellent. (4) Among the sciences honored to be a refuge of intellects for manifesting truth, this science is dignified. Therefore, I selected this subject for writing the book. Conjoining a declarative sentence to a performative sentence: Question: In 'wa ba'd', the waw is a conjunction, and the sentence after it is conjoined to what precedes it, i.e. 'al-hamd' and 'al-salah', and this conjunction is not correct because the sentence after 'wa ba'd' is declarative (khabariyyah), while 'al-hamd' and 'al-salah' are performative (insha'iyyah) sentences, so it would necessitate 'conjoining a declarative to a performative', and this is not permissible. Answer (1): Just as the sentence after the waw is declarative, likewise the sentence before the waw is also declarative, because in 'al-hamdu lillah', information is given that Allah deserves praise, and in 'wa al-salah', information is given that the Prophet (peace be upon him) deserves blessings and peace. So this is 'conjoining a declarative to a declarative'. Thus there is no objection. Answer (2): This is of the type 'conjoining a story to a story', i.e. it is not the conjunction of a sentence to a sentence, but the conjunction of the content after the waw to the content before it. Answer: This objection would arise if the waw were a conjunction, whereas we say it is a substitute waw (waw 'iwadiyyah) mentioned in place of 'amma' (as for).
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a prefatory introduction from the commentary 'Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. It begins with the basmalah and hamdalah, then explains the meaning of the word 'alam' in the context of the author's role as a guide. The commentator provides a glossary of key terms from the text (e.g., 'alam, dirayah, mabsut, etc.), clarifying their meanings. Then, in the section 'Tamhidi Muqaddimah', it outlines the standard practice of authors in their introductions: stating the reason for choosing the subject, the purpose of writing, the qualities of the book, and additionally for a commentator, the reason for selecting the specific text. Next, under 'Aghrad' (Objectives), the commentator focuses on the first part: 'Illat Ta'yin al-Fann' (Reason for Specifying the Subject). He explains that Allamah Taftazani gave four reasons for choosing usul al-fiqh: (1) it combines rational and transmitted evidences; (2) it enables deriving rulings not explicitly mentioned (preparing for ijtihad); (3) it is the most excellent discipline for strengthening Sharia rulings; (4) it is dignified as a refuge for intellects in manifesting truth. Finally, the passage addresses a grammatical issue: the conjunction of 'wa ba'd' to the preceding 'al-hamd wa al-salah'. Some object that this is 'conjoining a declarative sentence to a performative sentence', which is grammatically impermissible. The commentator provides two answers: first, both sentences are actually declarative because they give information about deserving praise and blessings; second, the waw is not a conjunction but a substitute for 'amma', so the issue does not arise. This showcases the linguistic rigor of the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
علت تعیین فن (illat ta'yin al-fann): The reason for choosing a particular discipline for writing a book; in this passage, the author gives four reasons for selecting usul al-fiqh.
عطف الخبر على الانشاء (atf al-khabar 'ala al-insha'): Conjoining a declarative sentence (khabar) to a performative/constructive sentence (insha'), which is considered grammatically impermissible. The commentator argues that both sentences here are actually declarative.
تمہیدی مقدمہ (tamhidi muqaddimah): Preliminary introduction; the standard elements an author includes at the beginning of a book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many reasons does Taftazani give for selecting usul al-fiqh?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Taftazani gives four reasons for choosing usul al-fiqh: it integrates rational and transmitted proofs, enables ijtihad, strengthens sharia, and is a dignified refuge for intellects.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
12 min
Resolving a Grammatical Issue: 'Atf al-Khabar 'ala al-Insha'
Grammatical analysis of the transitional phrase 'wa ba'd'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the grammatical objection concerning 'wa ba'd' and the two responses provided by the commentator.

Core Idea
Careful grammatical analysis protects the coherence of legal arguments.

The passage addresses a potential grammatical flaw in the author's transition from the hamdalah to 'wa ba'd'. Understanding the resolution demonstrates the linguistic precision required in usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
The conjunction (waw) in 'wa ba'd' is joining a declarative sentence (ba'd) to a performative sentence (al-hamd wa al-salah), which is grammatically impermissible.
Performative = insha', declarative = khabar.
2
First response: both are declarative
The commentator argues that 'al-hamdu lillah' and 'wa al-salah' are actually declarative because they give information about Allah and the Prophet being deserving of praise and blessings.
Thus it is 'atf al-khabar 'ala al-khabar'.
3
Second response: waw is not a conjunction
The waw is not 'atf' but 'waw 'iwadiyyah' substituted for 'amma' (as for), so no conjunction of sentences occurs.
This avoids the issue entirely.
4
Evaluate the responses
Both responses show the commentator's linguistic skill in defending the text against potential criticism.

عطف الخبر على الانشاء
سوال:۔ و بعد میں واؤ عاطفہ ہے اور مابعد کا جملہ کے ماقبل یعنی الحمد و الصلوۃ پر عطف ہے اور یہ عطف درست نہیں کیونکہ وبعد کا مابعد جملہ خبریہ ہے اور الحمد والصلوۃ یہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے تو لازم آئے گا " عطف الخبر علی الانشاء “ اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۱):۔ جس طرح واؤ کا مابعد جملہ خبریہ ہے اسی طرح واؤ کا ماقبل بھی جملہ خبریہ ہے کیونکہ الحمدللہ میں اللہ کے حمد کے مستحق ہونے کی خبر دی گئی ہے اور والصلوۃ میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مستحق صلوۃ و سلام ہو نے کی خبر دی گئی ہے تو یہ عطف الخبر علی الخبر “ ہے۔ فلا اعتراض ۔ جواب (۲) : ۔ یہ عطف القصہ علی القصہ کے قبیل سے ہے یعنی جملہ کا عطف جملہ پر نہیں بلکہ واؤ کے بعد کے مضمون کا (۲):۔ القصہ ماقبل کے مضمون پر عطف ہے۔ جواب : یہ سوال تب وارد ہوتا جب واو عاطفہ ہو حالانکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ واؤ عوضیہ ہے اما شرطیہ کے عوض میں اس کو ذکر
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon the master of the messengers. Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih slaughters every issue, i.e. dominates every issue. 71: 'Alam: It has two meanings (1) a flag: just as a flag is made a sign to find the way, likewise the author is a sign for guidance in religion (2) a mountain: just as mountains are used as landmarks to find the way, likewise the author is a sign for guidance. 'Alim meaning world. Dirayat meaning understanding. Mu'addil meaning straightener. Munqih: cleanser. Aghsan is plural of ghusn meaning branch. Mabsut: large book. Mustasfa: summary, essence. Madid: long. Wajiz: brief. Arkan: plural of rukn. Waf: adjective after adjective meaning complete, nothing left. Wasit: intermediate. Mabani is plural of mabna meaning foundation. Salaka yasluku sulukan: to walk. Minhajan: path. Badi'an: wondrous. Asrar: plural of sirr meaning secret. Istawla: from bab isti'fal meaning to ascend. Al-Amad: meaning limit. Al-Aqsa: utmost. Manar: in ancient times they built pillars to determine the road and lit fire on them at night so that no one would forget the road; now it is used in the absolute sense of pillar. Masabtaha: from bab nasr meaning small. Ratq: veil. Afkar: plural of fikr. Fatq: meaning opening. Adhan: plural of udhun meaning ear. Preliminary Introduction: Generally, authors are accustomed to stating the following matters at the beginning of their book: (1) the reason for specifying the subject, i.e. they explain why this subject was chosen for the book; (2) the purpose of authorship, i.e. they state the goal of writing the book; (3) the quality of the book, i.e. they describe the characteristics of their book and its style; (4) and if the author is a commentator, in addition to the above matters, he also mentions the reason for choosing the book and the text, i.e. why he selected this particular text for commentary. Objectives: This passage has three parts. Now we will state the purpose of each part, and along with that we will also mention some questions and answers related to each part. Reason for specifying the subject: His saying 'Wa ba'd': The purpose of the commentator in this phrase, Allamah Taftazani, has explained the reason for specifying the subject, that he selected this subject for writing the book for several reasons: (1) This science encompasses rational and transmitted matters; Quran and hadith are from the transmitted category, and ijma' and qiyas are from the rational category. Similarly, some things are known by rational proofs, e.g. the authority of the Book of Allah, and some things are known by transmitted proofs, e.g. most rulings. (2) Through this science, knowledge of non-derived issues is obtained, i.e. this science develops the capacity for ijtihad. (3) Among the sciences accepted for strengthening the rulings of Sharia, this science is the most excellent. (4) Among the sciences honored to be a refuge of intellects for manifesting truth, this science is dignified. Therefore, I selected this subject for writing the book. Conjoining a declarative sentence to a performative sentence: Question: In 'wa ba'd', the waw is a conjunction, and the sentence after it is conjoined to what precedes it, i.e. 'al-hamd' and 'al-salah', and this conjunction is not correct because the sentence after 'wa ba'd' is declarative (khabariyyah), while 'al-hamd' and 'al-salah' are performative (insha'iyyah) sentences, so it would necessitate 'conjoining a declarative to a performative', and this is not permissible. Answer (1): Just as the sentence after the waw is declarative, likewise the sentence before the waw is also declarative, because in 'al-hamdu lillah', information is given that Allah deserves praise, and in 'wa al-salah', information is given that the Prophet (peace be upon him) deserves blessings and peace. So this is 'conjoining a declarative to a declarative'. Thus there is no objection. Answer (2): This is of the type 'conjoining a story to a story', i.e. it is not the conjunction of a sentence to a sentence, but the conjunction of the content after the waw to the content before it. Answer: This objection would arise if the waw were a conjunction, whereas we say it is a substitute waw (waw 'iwadiyyah) mentioned in place of 'amma' (as for).
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a prefatory introduction from the commentary 'Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. It begins with the basmalah and hamdalah, then explains the meaning of the word 'alam' in the context of the author's role as a guide. The commentator provides a glossary of key terms from the text (e.g., 'alam, dirayah, mabsut, etc.), clarifying their meanings. Then, in the section 'Tamhidi Muqaddimah', it outlines the standard practice of authors in their introductions: stating the reason for choosing the subject, the purpose of writing, the qualities of the book, and additionally for a commentator, the reason for selecting the specific text. Next, under 'Aghrad' (Objectives), the commentator focuses on the first part: 'Illat Ta'yin al-Fann' (Reason for Specifying the Subject). He explains that Allamah Taftazani gave four reasons for choosing usul al-fiqh: (1) it combines rational and transmitted evidences; (2) it enables deriving rulings not explicitly mentioned (preparing for ijtihad); (3) it is the most excellent discipline for strengthening Sharia rulings; (4) it is dignified as a refuge for intellects in manifesting truth. Finally, the passage addresses a grammatical issue: the conjunction of 'wa ba'd' to the preceding 'al-hamd wa al-salah'. Some object that this is 'conjoining a declarative sentence to a performative sentence', which is grammatically impermissible. The commentator provides two answers: first, both sentences are actually declarative because they give information about deserving praise and blessings; second, the waw is not a conjunction but a substitute for 'amma', so the issue does not arise. This showcases the linguistic rigor of the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
علت تعیین فن (illat ta'yin al-fann): The reason for choosing a particular discipline for writing a book; in this passage, the author gives four reasons for selecting usul al-fiqh.
عطف الخبر على الانشاء (atf al-khabar 'ala al-insha'): Conjoining a declarative sentence (khabar) to a performative/constructive sentence (insha'), which is considered grammatically impermissible. The commentator argues that both sentences here are actually declarative.
تمہیدی مقدمہ (tamhidi muqaddimah): Preliminary introduction; the standard elements an author includes at the beginning of a book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second response to the grammatical objection concerning 'wa ba'd'?
A) The waw is a performative conjunction.
B) The waw is a substitute for 'amma'.
C) The sentence is actually performative.
D) The issue is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The commentator resolves the grammatical issue by arguing either that both sentences are declarative or that the waw is not a conjunction but a substitute for 'amma'.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Why the Author Chose Usul al-Fiqh
Explains why the author chose usul al-fiqh as his subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four reasons the author gives for selecting usul al-fiqh as his subject and explain how these reasons highlight the discipline's unique combination of rational and transmitted sources.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh uniquely fuses transmitted and rational sources to empower ijtihad and strengthen Shari’ah.

In this introductory passage, the distinguished scholar Allamah Taftazani lays out his deliberate rationale for writing a treatise on usul al-fiqh. Rather than a casual choice, he presents four compelling reasons that reveal the discipline’s comprehensive nature and its pivotal role in Islamic legal theory. As you read, notice how he frames usul al-fiqh as both a transmitter of revealed truths and a tool for rational derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first reason – comprehensiveness
The author states that usul al-fiqh combines 'ma'qulat' (rational) and 'manqulat' (transmitted) matters. The Qur'an and Hadith are transmitted, while Ijma' and Qiyas are rational.
This shows the discipline's dual nature.
2
Recognize the second reason – preparing for ijtihad
He says it provides knowledge of non-derived issues, i.e., it cultivates the capacity for independent legal reasoning.
Usul is foundational for a mujtahid.
3
Examine the third reason – excellence in strengthening Shari'ah
Among accepted sciences, usul al-fiqh is the most excellent for consolidating legal rulings.
It gives firm grounding to fiqh.
4
Consider the fourth reason – honor as a refuge for intellects
For manifesting truth, it is honorable as a shelter for rational minds.
The author values its intellectual prestige.

قولہ وبعد : غرض شاریخ اس عبارت میں علامہ تفتازانی نے وجہ تعیین فن کو بیان فرمایا ہے کہ کتاب کو لکھنے کے لئے میں نے اس فن کو کئی وجوہ سے متعین کیا (۱) یہ علم معقولات اور منقولات کو جامع ہے کہ قرآن وحدیث منقول کے قبیل سے ہیں اور اجماع اور قیاس معقول کے قبیل سے ہیں اسی طرح بعض چیزیں دلائل عقلیہ سے معلوم ہوتی ہیں مثلا کتاب اللہ کا حجت ہونا اور بعض چیزوں کا علم دلائل نقلیہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے جیسے اکثر احکام (۲) اس علم سے مسائل غیر مستنبطہ کا علم حاصل ہوتا ہے گویا کہ اس علم سے اجتہاد کی استعداد پیدا ہوتی ہے (۳) احکام شریعت کو مضبوط کرنے کے لئے جن علوم کو قبولیت حاصل ہے ان سب سے یہ علم افضل ہے (۴) اظہار حق کے لئے جن علوم کو عقلوں کی پناہ گاہ ہونے کا شرف حاصل ہے ان میں سے یہ علم باعزت ہے اس لئے میں نے کتاب لکھنے کے لئے اس فن کو منتخب کیا۔
He said: 'After (amma ba'd):' The intention of the commentator in this expression: Allamah Taftazani has explained the reason for specifying the subject – that for writing the book I specified this subject for several reasons: (1) This science combines rational and transmitted matters – the Qur'an and Hadith are from the transmitted category, while Ijma' and Qiyas are from the rational category. Similarly, some things are known through rational proofs, e.g., the authority of the Book of Allah, and some things are known through transmitted proofs, like most rulings. (2) Through this science, knowledge of non-derived issues is obtained; i.e., this science prepares one for Ijtihad. (3) Among the sciences that are accepted for strengthening the rulings of Shari'ah, this science is the most excellent. (4) Among the sciences that have the honor of being a refuge for intellects for manifesting the truth, this science is honorable. Therefore I chose this subject for writing the book.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary by the author on the reason for choosing the discipline of usul al-fiqh. It is part of the introduction where Taftazani justifies his choice. The four reasons are: 1) It combines rational and transmitted sources, covering both Qur'an/Hadith (transmitted) and Ijma'/Qiyas (rational). 2) It develops the capacity for ijtihad by enabling derivation of new rulings. 3) It is the most excellent science for strengthening Shari'ah rulings. 4) It is honorable as a refuge for intellects in manifesting truth. The author concludes by stating his selection of this subject.

Key Terms
تعیین فن (ta'yin al-fann): Specification of the discipline (usul al-fiqh) as the subject of the work.
معقولات و منقولات (ma'qulat wa manqulat): Rational matters and transmitted matters. Here, the Qur'an and Hadith are transmitted, while Ijma' and Qiyas are rational.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The author selected usul al-fiqh because it uniquely weaves together transmitted revelation and rational analysis to empower ijtihad and fortify the Shari'ah.

Criteria for Selecting a Classical Text: Author Merit and Comprehensiveness
Justifies selection of Tanqih/Tawdih as the text for commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria used by classical Hanafi scholars to select a foundational usul text and apply these criteria to evaluate other texts within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar chooses a text for the author's unmatched mastery and the book's self-sufficiency, not mere brevity.

Why did the commentator choose Tanqih/Tawdih among many usul works? This passage reveals two explicit reasons: the unparalleled scholarly rank of the author (Sadr al-Shari'ah) and the text's concise comprehensiveness (jami' mani'). Understanding these criteria is a key methodology in Hanafi scholarship, teaching us how to weigh authority and utility in selecting a primary source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first criterion: Author's Virtue
Locate the phrase 'اس کتاب کا مصنف کئی خوبیوں کا مالک ہے'. Understand that one reason is the personal scholarly excellence of the author, which is considered unmatched in this field.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on scholarly lineage and authority (thiqah) in accepting texts.
2
Identify the second criterion: Comprehensiveness
Find the description 'مختصر اور جامع مانع'. Recognize that the text is praised for being concise yet covering all essential topics, thus eliminating the need for other books.
Jami' mani' is a technical term meaning a text that gathers what is needed and prevents gaps.
3
Reflect on the application
Consider why these criteria matter in studying usul al-fiqh: a reliable author ensures correct derivation; a comprehensive text saves time and provides systematic coverage.
This method mirrors how Hanafi jurists evaluate hadith collections or fiqh manuals.

قولہ وان کتاب لاتی ، غرض شارح:۔ اس عبارت میں شائع نے علت تعین متن کوڈ کر کو کیا ہے کہ میں نے شرح لکھنے کے لئے اصول فقہ کے اس متن (تنقیح و توضیح ) کو منتخب کیوں کیا ؟ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی بھی کئی وجوہ ہیں (۱) اس کتاب کا مصنف کئی خوبیوں کا مالک ہے اور اس کو جو علمی کمال حاصل ہے کسی اور کو اس فن میں اتنا کمال حاصل نہیں ہے (۲) یہ کتاب ایسی مختصر اور جامع مانع ہے کہ جس میں اس فن کی چھوٹی اور بڑی کتاب کا خلاصہ موجود ہے اس کے ہوتے ہوئے اس فن کی کسی اور کتاب کی ضرورت نہیں رہتی۔

The intention of the commentator: In this expression, the commentator has explained the reason for specifying the text – that for writing a commentary, why did I select this text of usul al-fiqh (Tanqih and Tawdih)? He states that there are also several reasons: (1) The author of this book possesses many virtues, and the scholarly perfection he has is not attained by anyone else in this discipline to such an extent. (2) This book is so concise and comprehensive that it contains the summary of both small and large books of this discipline; with it, no other book of this discipline is needed.

Commentary
This passage continues the introduction, now explaining why the specific text (Tanqih and Tawdih) was chosen for commentary. Two reasons are given: the unique excellence of the author (Sadi al-Shari'ah?), and the book's comprehensiveness despite brevity, making it self-sufficient. This highlights respect for scholarly authority and practical utility in selecting a text for teaching or commentary.

Key Terms
متن تنقیح و توضیح (matn al-tanqih wa al-tawdih): The core text of usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shari'ah, used as the basis for Taftazani's commentary.
جامع مانع (jami' mani'): Comprehensive and protective; meaning the text covers all essential topics and prevents the need for other works.

Key Takeaway
A classical text is chosen for the author's expertise and the text's self-contained completeness, not merely brevity or fame.

Author’s Motivation and Defense: Selecting Tanqih and Responding to Critics
Author explains reasons for choosing Tanqih and defends against accusations of exaggeration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the reasons an author selects a base text for commentary and analyze the use of kinayah and grammatical conjunction (atf al-masdar) as tools for defending textual claims in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
An author defends his choice by citing the text’s perfection and conciseness, using kinayah to resolve linguistic objections.

In this introductory passage, the author of Al-Tarwih explains why he chose the text of Tanqih (and its commentary Tawdih) for his own commentary. He lists the unmatched scholarly rank of its author and the book's comprehensive conciseness. Anticipating accusations of exaggeration, he specifies four objective merits. He then clarifies a potential linguistic ambiguity—how 'lack of hearing' can mean 'lack of understanding'—by invoking the concept of kinayah. Finally, he applies the rule of Allama Radhi on the conjunction of a verbal noun to a sentence to affirm the book's extraordinary fame. This front matter sets the stage for the commentator's approach and demonstrates how subtle linguistic analysis is integral to usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's motivations
Read the first part of the passage to list the reasons given for selecting the text: the author's unique perfection and the book's comprehensive conciseness.
This establishes the authority of the base text.
2
Analyze the defense against exaggeration
Examine the four specific merits the author cites to prove his praise is factual, not hyperbolic.
The author is responding to a presumed critic.
3
Understand the use of kinayah
Focus on the objection about 'عدم سماع' (lack of hearing) and how the author explains it is a metaphorical expression for 'lack of knowledge'.
Kinayah is a key concept in Hanafi usul for interpreting indirect expressions.
4
Apply the rule of atf al-masdar
Study the rule from Allama Radhi that a masdar conjoined by waw to a sentence serves as emphasis, and see how it is applied to the phrase about the book's fame.
This grammatical analysis is used to strengthen the author's argument.

نعم قد سلک : غرض شاریخ :۔ اس عبارت میں شارع نے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔
سوال :۔ آپ تنقیح کی اتنی تعریفیں کرہے ہیں کہیں یہ مبالغہ آرائی اور کذب بیانی تو نہیں؟
جواب :- شاریخ نے جواب دیا کہ میری باتیں مبالغہ پر محمول نہیں ہیں بلکہ حقیقت پر محمول ہیں اور اس کتاب میں ایسی خصوصیات ہیں جن کی وجہ سے میں تعریف کرنے پر مجبور ہوا ہوں اور وہ خصوصیات یہ ہیں (۱) مصنف نے تحقیق کے میدان میں انوکھا انداز ( طرز ) اختیار کیا ہے (۲) تدقیق کی آخری حد کو چھونے لگا کہ اس سے آگے کوئی جا بھی نہیں سکتا (۳) مصنف نے اس کتاب میں اپنی طرف سے زائد فوائد بیان کیے ہیں جو صرف ان کی فکر و بصیرت کا نتیجہ ہیں کسی اور اصولی نے ان کو سوچا تک نہیں (۴) ایسے نکات بیان کیے ہیں کہ ان کو اہل عقل نے آج تک سنا ہی نہیں لہذا جو کچھ میں نے کہا یہ کوئی مبالغہ آرائی نہیں ہے۔
قوله ما فتق بها رتق اذانهم : سوال:۔ اس عبارت سے تو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اولوالا بھار نے ان نکات کو سنا ہی نہیں حالانکہ مقصود یہ ہے کہ اولوالا بصار نے ان نکات کو سمجھا نہیں۔ تو شاریخ کی یہ عبارت مقصود پر دال نہیں ہے۔ جواب :۔ عدم سماع کنایہ ہے عدم علم اور عدم اور اک سے کیونکہ عام طور پر اس قسم کے نکات کا علم سماغ سے تعلق رکھتا ہے گویا .
کہ ان نکات کے علم کو سماع لازم ہے تو شاریخ نے لازم بول کر لزوم مراد لیا ہے یعنی ذکر تو نفی سماع کا کیا ہے اور مرا دلیا ہے نفی علم کو اور کو کنا یہ کہتے ہیں اور کنایہ کا استعمال کلام عرب میں کثیر ہے لہذا یہ عبارت مقصود پر دال ہے فلا اشکال۔
عطف المصدر علی الجملہ کے بارے میں علامہ رضی کا ضابطہ
قوله ولا اشتهار في نصف النهار : ضابطہ :۔ علامہ رضی نے ایک ضابطہ نقل کیا ہے کہ جب مصدرکا کسی جملہ پر عطف بواسطہ واؤ کے ہو تو وہ معطوف علیہ کی تاکید کے لئے آتا ہے اور اس کے فعل کو حذف کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے کیونکہ معطوف علیہ اس کے فعل مقدر پر دلالت کرتا ہے جیسے ” اعتديت ولا اعتداء الغراب “اى” لا اعتديت اعتداء الغراب بل اسرع منه تو اسی طرح یہاں ولا اشتہار الشمس کا عطف ہے طار" پر جو اشتہر “ کے معنی میں ہے تو تقدیر عبارت ہوگی لا اشتهر اشتهار الشمس بل اشهر منه ، مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ کتاب نصف النہار کے سورج کی طرح مشہور نہیں ہوئی بلکہ اس سے بھی زیادہ مشہور ہوئی ہے۔ یا واؤ حالیہ ہے اور اشتہار منصوب بنزع الخافض ہے اصل میں تھا ولا کاشتھار الشمس في نصف النهار معنی ہوگا کہ یہ کتاب مشہور ہوئی ہے حال یہ ہے کہ نصف النہار میں سورج کے مشہور ہونے کی طرح نہیں بلکہ اس سے بھی زیادہ مشہور ہوئی۔
وَلَقَدْ صَادَفَتُ مُجْتَازِى بِمَا وَرَاءَ النَّهرِ لِكَثِيرٍ مِن فُضَلَاءِ الدَّهْرِ أَفْئِدَةً تَهْوِى إِلَيْهِ وَأَكبَادًا هَائِمَةٌ عَلَيْهِ وَعُقُولًا جَاثِيَةٌ بَينَ يَدَيهِ وَرَغْبَاتٍ مُستَوقِفَةٌ بِالمَطَايَا لَدَيهِ مُعتَصِمِينَ فِي كَشفِ أَستَارِهِ بِالحَوَاشِي وَالْأَطْرَافِ قَانِعِينَ فِي بِحَارٍ أَسْرَارِهِ عَنِ اللَّالِى بِالْأَصْدَافِ لَا تَحُلُّ أَنَامِلُ الْانظَارِ عُقَدَ مُعَضَلَاتِهِ وَلَا يَفْتَحُ بَنَانُ البَيَانِ أَبوَابَ مُعْلَقَاتِـهِ فَلَطَائِفَهُ بَعْدُ تَحتَ حُجُبِ الألفَاظِ مَستَورَةٌ وَخَرَايْدُهُ فِي خِيَامٍ الأستَارِ مَقصُورَةٌ تَرى حَوَالَيْهَا هِمَمًا مُستَشرِفَةَ الْأَعْنَاقِ وَدُونَ الوُصُولِ إِلَيْهَا أَعْيُنًا سَاهِرَةَ الأحدَاقِ فَأُمِرُتْ بِلِسَانِ الإِلهَامِ لَا كَوَهِم مِن الْأُوهَامِ أَن أَخُوضَ فِي لجَج فَوَائِدِهِ وَأَعُوضَ عَلَى عُرَرٍ فَرَائِدِهِ وَأنشُرَ مَطوِيَّاتِ رُمُوزِهِ وَأَظْهِرَ مَحْفِيَّاتِ كُنُوزِهِ وَأُسَهْلَ مَسَالِكَ شِعَابِهِ وَأُذَلَّلَ شَوَارِدَ صِعَابِهِ بِحَيثُ يَصِيرُ المَتنُ مَشرُوحًا وَيَزِيدُ الشَّرحُ بَيَانًا وَوُضُوحًا فَطَفِقْتُ أَفْتَحِمُ مَوَارِدَ السَّهرِ فِى ظُلَمِ الدَّيَاجِرِ وَأَحتَمِلُ مَكَابِدَ الفكرِ فِى ظَمَلِ الهَوَاجِرِ رَاكِبًا كُلَّ صَعِبٍ وَذَلُولٍ
It has been done, this is the reason that later 'فان' and 'فاجزا' are here, so no objection. Reason for selecting the text. His statement: 'وان کتاب لاتی', purpose of the commentator: In this phrase, the author coded the reason for selecting the text: why did I choose this text (Tanqih and Tawdih) of usul al-fiqh for writing a commentary? He says there are several reasons: (1) The author of this book possesses many virtues and has such scholarly perfection that no one else in this field has attained such perfection; (2) This book is so concise and comprehensive that it contains the summary of all books—small and large—of this discipline, so with its existence, there is no need for any other book in this field. The doubt of exaggeration and its removal. 'Na'am qad salaka': purpose of the commentator: In this phrase, the commentator answers a presumed question. Question: You are praising Tanqih so much, could this be exaggeration and falsehood? Answer: The commentator replied that my words are not to be taken as exaggeration but as truth, and this book has such characteristics that forced me to praise it, and those characteristics are: (1) The author adopted a unique style in the field of research; (2) He reached the ultimate limit of precision such that no one can go beyond; (3) The author added extra benefits in this book that are the result of his own thought and insight, which no other usuli even thought of; (4) He presented such points that the people of intellect have never heard before. Therefore, what I said is not exaggeration. His statement: 'ma fataqa biha ratqa adhanihim': Question: This phrase indicates that the people of insight never heard these points, whereas the intended meaning is that they did not understand them. So the commentator's phrase does not indicate the intended meaning. Answer: 'عدم سماع' (lack of hearing) is a metaphor for lack of knowledge and lack of comprehension because generally knowledge of such points is related to hearing. So the commentator mentioned the necessary (lazim) and intended the condition of necessity (luzum), meaning he mentioned the negation of hearing and intended the negation of knowledge. This is called kinayah, and the use of kinayah is abundant in Arabic speech. Therefore, this phrase indicates the intended meaning, so no problem. The rule of Allama Radhi regarding conjuncting the verbal noun (masdar) to a sentence. His statement: 'Wa la ishtiharu fi nisf al-nahar': Rule: Allama Radhi transmitted a rule that when a masdar is conjoined to a sentence by the letter waw, it comes to emphasize the conjoined item, and deleting its verb is obligatory because the conjoined item indicates its implied verb. For example: 'I'tadaytu wa la i'tidaa' al-ghurab', meaning 'I did not do the injustice of a crow but faster than it.' Similarly, here 'wa la ishtihara al-shams' is conjoined to 'tara' which is in the meaning of 'ishtahara'. So the implied expression would be 'la ishtahara ishtihara al-shams bal ashharu minhu'. The meaning is that this book did not become famous like the sun at noon, but became even more famous than that. Or the waw is circumstantial (waw al-haliyyah) and 'ishtihar' is accusative due to removal of the preposition; originally it was 'wa la ka-ishtihari al-shamsi fi nisf al-nahar'. The meaning would be that this book became famous, while it is not like the fame of the sun at noon, but even more famous than that. And indeed I encountered, while passing through beyond the river, for many of the eminent scholars of the time, hearts yearning towards it, livers smitten with love for it, intellects kneeling before it, and desires halting their mounts at its door, clinging to unveiling its veils with glosses and commentaries, contented in the seas of its secrets from pearls with shells. The fingers of glances cannot untie the knots of its difficulties, and the fingers of eloquence cannot open the doors of its intricate problems. Its subtleties are still veiled under the curtains of words, and its virgins are secluded in the tents of covers. You see around it aspirations stretching their necks, and before reaching it eyes sleepless. So I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration—not by a weak fancy—to plunge into the depths of its benefits and dive for the pearls of its unique gems, to unfold the folded secrets of its symbols and manifest the hidden treasures of its stores, to smoothen the paths of its rugged ways and tame the refractory difficulties thereof, so that the text becomes explained and the commentary increases in clarity and lucidity. Then I began to force open the sources of sleeplessness in the darkness of the nights and endure the hardships of thought in the heat of noons, riding every rough and smooth [path].
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (front matter) in which he explains his motivation for selecting the text of Tanqih (by Sadr al-Sharia) and the subsequent Tawdih for his commentary (Al-Tarwih). He gives two reasons: the author's unmatched scholarly perfection and the book's comprehensive conciseness (jami' mani'). He then defends himself against potential accusations of exaggeration by listing four specific merits of the book, emphasizing that his praise is factual. Next, he addresses a linguistic objection regarding a phrase, explaining that 'lack of hearing' is a kinayah (metonymy) for 'lack of knowledge'—a common device in Arabic. Finally, he presents the rule of Allama Radhi about the conjunction of a masdar (verbal noun) to a sentence, applying it to the phrase 'wa la ishtiharu fi nisf al-nahar' to argue that the book's fame surpasses that of the sun at noon. The passage concludes with a eloquent Arabic description of the book's reception and the author's divine inspiration to write the commentary, highlighting his arduous effort. The discussion is purely introductory and does not yet enter into substantive usul rulings.

Key Terms
علت تعيين متن (Illat ta'yin al-matn): The reason or motivation for selecting a particular text for commentary.
کنایہ (Kinayah): A word or phrase used indirectly to imply something else, relying on context.
عطف المصدر على الجملة (Atf al-masdar 'ala al-jumla): Conjoining a verbal noun (masdar) to a complete sentence using waw, where the masdar emphasizes the sentence's meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's main defense against the accusation that his praise of Tanqih is exaggeration?
A) He admits exaggeration is necessary for promotion.
B) He lists four specific, factual merits of the book.
C) He changes the subject to criticize his critics.
D) He quotes approval from other scholars.

Key Takeaway
An author's defense of his text selection relies on both substantive merits and precise linguistic tools (like kinayah and grammatical rules) to preempt and resolve objections.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Author's Preface: Motivation and Methodology
Author's preface describing motivation and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's claim of divine inspiration as motivation, distinguish it from mere delusion, and describe the methodological steps he undertook in writing his commentary.

Core Idea
Scholarly work must be rooted in true inspiration, not whimsy.

In this preface, the author sets the stage for his commentary by describing the intellectual hunger for the base text and his personal calling to unlock its secrets. His account of inspiration and effort provides a window into the classical scholarly ethos.

Guided Path
1
Locate the context
Identify where the author was (Ma wara al-nahr / Transoxiana) and what he observed: many scholars were deeply attached to the base book but struggled with its difficulties.
Ma wara al-nahr is a key center of Hanafi learning.
2
Recognize the motivation
Note that the author claims he was commanded by 'the tongue of inspiration (ilham)' – not by delusion – to write the commentary. This distinguishes genuine motivation from ego.
In usul al-fiqh, ilham is not a legal source, but it is valid for personal scholarly drive.
3
List the author's tasks
The author lists: plunge into the benefits, dive for gems, unfold symbols, bring forth treasures, make paths easy, tame difficulties.
These metaphors describe meticulous scholarly work.
4
Observe the method
He describes working day and night, enduring hardship, riding every mount – i.e., using all available resources to master the principles (usul).
This reflects the high standard of Hanafi scholarly discipline.
5
Identify the goal
The ultimate aim: make the matn clear and remove doubts from its 'brides' (the hidden gems).
Clarity (wuduh) and explanation (bayan) are central.

Source Text

وَلَقَدْ صَادَفَتُ مُجْتَازِى بِمَا وَرَاءَ النَّهرِ لِكَثِيرٍ مِن فُضَلَاءِ الدَّهْرِ أَفْئِدَةً تَهْوِى إِلَيْهِ وَأَكبَادًا هَائِمَةٌ عَلَيْهِ وَعُقُولًا جَاثِيَةٌ بَينَ يَدَيهِ وَرَغْبَاتٍ مُستَوقِفَةٌ بِالمَطَايَا لَدَيهِ مُعتَصِمِينَ فِي كَشفِ أَستَارِهِ بِالحَوَاشِي وَالْأَطْرَافِ قَانِعِينَ فِي بِحَارٍ أَسْرَارِهِ عَنِ اللَّالِى بِالْأَصْدَافِ لَا تَحُلُّ أَنَامِلُ الْانظَارِ عُقَدَ مُعَضَلَاتِهِ وَلَا يَفْتَحُ بَنَانُ البَيَانِ أَبوَابَ مُعْلَقَاتِـهِ فَلَطَائِفَهُ بَعْدُ تَحتَ حُجُبِ الألفَاظِ مَستَورَةٌ وَخَرَايْدُهُ فِي خِيَامٍ الأستَارِ مَقصُورَةٌ تَرى حَوَالَيْهَا هِمَمًا مُستَشرِفَةَ الْأَعْنَاقِ وَدُونَ الوُصُولِ إِلَيْهَا أَعْيُنًا سَاهِرَةَ الأحدَاقِ فَأُمِرُتْ بِلِسَانِ الإِلهَامِ لَا كَوَهِم مِن الْأُوهَامِ أَن أَخُوضَ فِي لحَج فَوَائِدِهِ وَأَعُوصَ عَلَى عُرَرٍ فَرَائِدِهِ وَأنشُرَ مَطوِيَّاتِ رُمُوزِهِ وَأَظْهِرَ مَحْفِيَّاتِ كُنُوزِهِ وَأُسَهْلَ مَسَالِكَ شِعَابِهِ وَأُذَلَّلَ شَوَارِدَ صِعَابِهِ بِحَيثُ يَصِيرُ المَتنُ مَشرُوحًا وَيَزِيدُ الشَّرحُ بَيَانًا وَوُضُوحًا فَطَفِقْتُ أَفْتَحِمُ مَوَارِدَ السَّهرِ فِى ظُلَمِ الدَّيَاجِرِ وَأَحتَمِلُ مَكَابِدَ الفكرِ فِى ظَمَلِ الهَوَاجِرِ رَاكِبًا كُلَّ صَعِبٍ وَذَلُولٍ لاقتِنَاصِ شَوَارِدِ الأُصُولِ وَنَازِفًا عُلالَةَ الْحِدْ فِي الْأُصُولِ إِلَى مَقَاصِدِ الْأَبْوَابِ وَالفُصُولِ حَتَّى اسْتَولَيتُ عَلَى الغَايَةِ القُصوى مِن أَسرَارِ الكِتَابِ وَأَمَطْتُ عَن وُجُوهِ خَرَائِدِهِ قِنَاعَ الْارْتِيَابِ
ترجمہ: اور تحقیق پایا میں نے اپنے گزرنے کے وقت ماوراء النہر کے علاقوں سے زمانے کے بہت سارے فضلاء کے دلوں کو کہ وہ اس کتاب کی طرف مائل ہیں اور جگروں کو کہ وہ اس پر حیران ہیں اور عقلوں کو کہ وہ اس کے سامنے گھٹنے ٹیکنے والی ہیں اور رغبتوں کو کہ وہ روکنے والی ہیں سواریوں کو اس کے پاس، چنگل مارنے والی ہیں اس کتاب کے پردوں کو کھولنے میں حواشی اور کناروں کے ساتھ ، قناعت کرنے والے ہیں، اس کتاب کے رازوں کے سمندروں میں موتیوں سے سیپیوں پر نہیں کھول سکتیں نظروں کی انگلیاں اس کتاب کی مشکلات کی گانٹھوں کو اور نہیں کھول سکتے بیان کے پورے اس کے بند در اوزوں کو ، پس اس کی باریکیاں بعد اس کے ( لکھنے سے لے کر اب تک ) الفاظ کے پردوں کے نیچے چھپی ہوئی ہیں اور اسکی خوبر ومحبوبائیں پردوں کے خیموں میں بند ہیں، دیکھے گا تو اس کے اردگرد ہمتوں کو کہ وہ گرد نہیں اٹھانے والی ہیں اور ان تک پہنچنے کے ورے دیکھے گا تو آنکھوں کو کہ وہ پتلیوں کو جگانے والی ہیں پس مجھے حکم دیا گیا الہام کی زبان سے نہ کہ اوہام میں سے کسی وہم کے ساتھ یہ کہ داخل ہو جاؤں اس کتاب کے فوائد کی موجوں میں اور غوطے لگاؤں اس کے یکتا موتیوں کے بڑے بڑے حوضوں میں اور کھول دوں اس کے لیٹے ہوئے اشارات کو ظاہر کر دوں اس سے مخفی خزانوں کو اور آسان کر دوں اسکی مشکل گزار راہوں کو اور فرمانبردار کر دوں اسکی مشکلات کے وحشی جانوروں کو اس حیثیت سے کہ متن واضح ہو جائے اور شرح کی خوب وضاحت ہو جائے پس میں شروع ہوا کہ داخل ہوتا تھا جاگنے کے گھاٹوں میں تاریک رات کے اندھیروں میں اور اٹھاتا تھا میں فکر کی تکلیفیں سخت گرمیوں کی دوپہر کی پیاس میں اس حال میں کہ سوار ہونے والا تھا ہر مشکل اور آسان سواری پر اصول فقہ کے وحشی جانوروں کو شکار کرنے کے لئے اور ختم کرنے والا تھا باقی ماندہ کوشش کو ابواب اور فصول کے مقاصد تک پہنچنے میں یہاں تک کہ میں چڑھ گیا مقصود کی انتہاء پر یعنی کتاب کے رازوں کے اور ہٹا دیا میں نے اس کتاب کی خوب رو محبوباؤں کے چہروں سے شک کے پردوں کو۔
تشریح:۔ اس عبارت کی تشریح میں تین امور بیان کیے جاتے ہیں (۱) لغوی تحقیق (۲) غرض شاریخ (۳) استعارات۔ امر اول لغوی تحقیق: صادفت باب مفاصلہ سے واحد متکلم ماضی معلوم کا صیغہ ہے وجدت کے معنی میں
And indeed I found, while passing by the regions beyond the river, many of the virtuous of the time: hearts inclining towards it, livers bewildered by it, minds kneeling before it, desires stopping the mounts at it, clinging to uncovering its veils with marginal notes and fringes, content in the seas of its secrets with pearls from shells. The fingers of glances do not untie the knots of its difficulties, nor does the fingertip of eloquence open the doors of its locked ones. So its subtleties after that are concealed under the veils of words, and its brides are confined in the tents of curtains. You see around it aspirations raising their necks, and beyond reaching them, eyes sleepless of pupils. Then I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration, not by any delusion among delusions, to plunge into the waves of its benefits, dive for the unique pearls of its gems, unfold the folded symbols, bring forth its hidden treasures, make easy the paths of its rugged ways, and tame the untamed difficult beasts, such that the matn becomes explained and the commentary increases in clarity and lucidity. So I began to enter the resources of sleeplessness in the darkness of the nights and endure the hardships of thought under the midday heat, riding every rough and smooth mount for capturing the untamed animals of the principles (usul) and exhausting the remaining effort in the principles towards the objectives of chapters and sections, until I attained the ultimate goal of the secrets of the book and removed from the faces of its brides the veil of doubt.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is the author's preface in which he describes the situation he found: many scholars beyond the Oxus (ما وراء النهر) were deeply attached to this book (likely Al-Tawdih), but its difficulties remained unresolved. He felt a divine inspiration (not mere imagination) to write a commentary that would unlock its secrets. He then describes his strenuous efforts, working day and night, to achieve this goal. This preface serves as a front matter for the commentary, explaining the motivation and method. The elaborate metaphorical style is typical of scholarly introductions. The Urdu translation and tashrih (elaboration) follow, with the tashrih beginning to explain specific words like 'صادفت'.

Key Terms
ما وراء النهر (Ma wara al-nahr): Transoxiana, the region beyond the Oxus river, central to Hanafi scholarship.
الهام (ilham): Divine inspiration, distinguished from mere delusion (وهم).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His own desire for fame.
B) The command of his teacher.
C) The tongue of inspiration (ilham), not delusion.
D) The request of his students.

Key Takeaway
The author's preface establishes that legitimate scholarly work requires both divine motivation (ilham) and rigorous personal effort.

Understanding the Author's Preface: Metaphorical Language in Classical Usul Texts
Author states his purpose and achievement in writing this commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret the metaphorical language used by a classical Hanafi usul author in his preface and identify his stated purpose.

Core Idea
The author's preface reveals his aim: to uncover the hidden gems of usul al-fiqh and remove doubt from its most difficult passages.

This passage is the author's introductory statement, where he uses elaborate metaphors to describe his work. Understanding these metaphors is key to grasping the author's self-perception and the value he places on his commentary. The author employs terms like 'shawārid' (rare gems) and 'kharāʾid' (beautiful virgins) to elevate the reader's expectation of the content.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metaphors
Read the Arabic passage and pinpoint the three key metaphorical terms: 'shawārid', 'ʿulālah', and 'kharāʾid'. Note how each is used in context.
These are not legal terms but literary devices.
2
Translate each metaphor into plain meaning
Convert each metaphor into a straightforward expression. For example, 'shawārid al-uṣūl' means 'the rare and subtle points of usul'. 'ʿulālah al-ḥadd' means 'the essence of the discipline's definitions'. 'Kharāʾid' refers to 'the beautiful and intricate passages of the book'.
This step demystifies the author's flowery language.
3
Synthesize the author's overall purpose
Combine the plain meanings to understand the author's stated mission: he wrote this commentary to gather scattered principles, present the core definitions, and clarify any doubts about the book's most challenging parts.
The author claims to have achieved the utmost goal of unraveling the book's secrets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لاقْتِنَاصِ شَوَارِدِ الأُصُولِ وَنَازِفًا عُلالَةَ الْحِدْ فِي الْأُصُولِ إِلَى مَقَاصِدِ الْأَبْوَابِ وَالفُصُولِ حَتَّى اسْتَوْلَيْتُ عَلَى الْغَايَةِ الْقُصْوَى مِنْ أَسْرَارِ الْكِتَابِ وَأَمَطْتُ عَنْ وُجُوهِ خَرَائِدِهِ قِنَاعَ الْارْتِيَابِ
For hunting the stray gems of the principles and presenting the honey of the limit in the principles to the aims of the chapters and sections, until I attained the utmost goal from the secrets of the book and removed from the faces of its beautiful virgins the veil of suspicion.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface, where he employs highly metaphorical language to describe his scholarly mission. He states that he undertook this commentary to capture the rare and scattered principles of usul al-fiqh and to present the essence (honey) of the discipline's limits (al-hadd) to the intended chapters and sections. He claims to have reached the ultimate level of understanding the book's secrets and to have unveiled any doubt surrounding its beautiful and difficult passages (the 'virgins'). This is typical of classical introductions, displaying the author's humility and the perceived difficulty of the work.

Key Terms
شوارِد (shawārid): The rare, stray, or scattered items; here, the subtle points of usul al-fiqh that are not widely known.
عُلالَة (ʿulālah): The remaining portion of milk; metaphorically, the essence or honey of something. Here, the author presents the 'honey' of the limit (al-hadd) in usul.
خَرَائِد (kharāʾid): Beautiful virgins; metaphorically, the intricate and beautiful passages of the book that are difficult to access.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The cover of ambiguity
D) The mask of difficulty

Key Takeaway
The author presents his commentary as a work that gathers scattered principles, distills the essence of definitions, and unveils the hidden beauties of usul al-fiqh.

The Purpose of a Hanafi Commentary
Author explains the motive for writing the commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of a sharh (commentary) in the Hanafi usul tradition and identify the pedagogical motive behind the author's work.

Core Idea
A commentary unlocks the hidden depth of a terse matn that surface reading cannot reach.

This passage is from the editor's introduction to a major commentary on Sadr al-Shariah's Tawdih. It reveals the essential function of a sharh in the Hanafi curriculum: not to repeat what is already apparent, but to illuminate what is obscure. The author presents his motivation as a question and answer, arguing that even a comprehensive text like Tanqih still requires explanation to make its subtle points accessible to students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question posed
The passage sets up a hypothetical objection: if Tanqih is already comprehensive and sufficient, why write a commentary? Locate this question in the text.
The question is implied: 'When Tanqih contained so many excellences... what was the need to write its commentary?'
2
Extract the author's answer
Find the reasons given for writing the commentary. The author mentions the precision of the texts, the absence of a proper commentary, reliance on glosses, and the inability to access deep meanings.
3
Analyse the pedagogical gap
The author distinguishes between apparent meaning (zahir) and hidden points (nukat, madamin). Understand that the gap between these two levels justified the commentary.
This distinction mirrors the Hanafi usul concept of dalala: the text may be clear in one dimension but requires elaboration for full understanding.
4
Connect to the Hanafi tradition
Recognise that this commentary is part of a long chain of sharh works that build on matn texts. Each layer adds clarity and resolves difficulties.
Examples: Sharh al-Maniyyah, Sharh al-Wiqayah, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امر ثانی غرض شاری :۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے علت تالیف کتاب (شرح) کو بیان کیا ہے لیکن اس کو سوال جواب کی شکل میں سمجھیں۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ جب تنقیح اتنی خوبیوں پر مشتمل تھی کہ یہ چھوٹی بڑی کتابوں کے خلاصہ کو شامل ہے اور اپنے ماسوا دوسری کتابوں سے بے پرواہ کرنے والی ہے تو پھر اس کی شرح لکھنے کی کیا ضرورت تھی؟ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ تنقیح اور توضیح انتہائی ادق کتاب تھی اس کی کوئی شرح نہ تھی لوگ اس کو حل کرنے کے لئے حواشی پر گزارہ کر رہے تھے جس کی وجہ سے ظاہری الفاظ تو سمجھ رہے تھے لیکن اس کے اندر جو نکات اور مضامین چھپے ہوئے تھے ان تک رسائی نہیں ہو رہی تھی اس لئے میں نے اس کی شرح لکھی تا کہ وہ نکات اور مضامین واضح ہو جائیں اور طلباء کی پریشانی دور ہو جائے اور علم کی پیاس بجھ جائے ۔
Second matter: Author's objective. In this expression, the commentator has stated the reason for writing the book (the commentary). But understand it in the form of a question and answer. Question: When 'Tanqih' contained so many excellences that it includes the summary of small and large books and makes one independent of other books besides itself, then what was the need to write its commentary? Answer: It is that 'Tanqih' and 'Tawdih' were extremely precise books; they had no commentary. People were relying on glosses to solve them, due to which they understood the apparent words but could not access the points and meanings hidden within. Therefore, I wrote this commentary so that those points and meanings become clear, and the students' distress is removed, and the thirst for knowledge is quenched.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section where the commentator (the author of this commentary) explains the reason for composing the work. He presents it as a question and answer: given that the original text (Tanqih al-Usul by Sadr al-Shariah) was already comprehensive and sufficient, why was a commentary needed? The answer is that both Tanqih and its super-commentary Tawdih were extremely subtle and difficult, and no full commentary existed. Students could grasp only the surface meanings through marginal notes (hawashi) but could not penetrate the deeper legal points (nukat) and content (madamin). The commentator wrote this work to unlock those hidden layers, relieve students' difficulty, and satisfy their intellectual thirst. This highlights the pedagogical purpose of the commentary: not to replace the original but to make its depths accessible. In the Hanafi tradition, such commentaries (shuruh) are essential for transmitting the full legal reasoning of the madhhab.

Key Terms
علت تالیف (illat al-ta'lif): The reason or motive for composing a book.
تنقیح (tanqih): Refers to 'Tanqih al-Usul' by Sadr al-Shariah, a foundational text on Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
توضیح (tawdih): Refers to 'Al-Tawdih' by Sadr al-Shariah, a commentary on his own Tanqih.
شارح (sharih): The commentator; the author of this commentary.
حواشی (hawashi): Glosses; marginal notes that explain individual words or phrases but do not provide a full commentary.
نکات (nukat): Subtle points; deeper meanings or legal insights.
مضامین (madamin): Contents; the substantive legal ideas embedded in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main problem that the commentary aimed to solve?
A) The original books contained many errors.
B) Students could not afford the original books.
C) Students understood only the apparent words and missed the hidden points.
D) The original books were too long and needed summarization.

Key Takeaway
A commentary is written not to correct or replace the original text, but to unlock its deeper layers and make its subtleties accessible to learners.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Reason for Writing the Commentary
Author explains motive for writing commentary in question-answer format.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific need that prompted the author to write the commentary and explain how it addresses the shortcomings of the original text.

Core Idea
A commentary becomes essential when the original text's inner meanings are inaccessible without explicit explanation.

In this passage from the front matter of the commentary al-Talwīḥ, the author explains why he undertook the task of writing a commentary on al-Tanqīḥ. He frames it as a question: given the excellence of the original, why a commentary? His answer reveals the pedagogical gap that motivated his work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hypothetical question
The author poses a question: since al-Tanqīḥ is so comprehensive and self-sufficient, what need is there for a commentary? Recognize the rhetorical device used to introduce the motive.
2
Extract the author's answer
The answer states that al-Tanqīḥ and al-Tawḍīḥ were extremely subtle and had no existing commentary. People relied on marginal notes and could only grasp the literal words, not the hidden insights.
This reveals the gap between outward understanding and deep comprehension.
3
Analyze the pedagogical need
Understand that the commentary was written to uncover the hidden points and subjects, relieve students' distress, and quench their thirst for knowledge. This is a direct response to the identified gap.
The author positions himself as a guide, not a critic.
4
Connect to the commentary's features
In the concluding Arabic paragraph, the author lists the commentary's aims: establish usul rules, edit nodes, explain objectives, multiply benefits, and provide expositions, verifications, directions, and classifications.
These features directly address the need for deeper understanding.
5
Relate to usul methodology
Reflect on how this mirrors the Hanafi usul practice: original texts (like al-Tanqīḥ) are often mujmal (concise), and a commentary serves as bayan (clarification) to make them accessible for deriving rulings.
This illustrates the chain of textual transmission and interpretation.

باب نصر سے غوطہ لگانا فرائد " جمع ہے فریدہ کی بمعنی بڑا موتی مطويات جمع ہے مطوبة کی بمعنی لپٹی ہوئی چیز " رموز جمع ہے رمز کی بمعنی اشارہ مسالک جمع ہے مسلک کی بمعنی راہ شعاب دشوار گزار گھاٹی [؟] شوارد جمع ہے شاردہ کی بمعنی دوحشی جانور " اقتحم ، فتعال سے بمعنی داخل ہوتا موارد جمع ہے مورد کی بمعنی جائے ورود دیاجو جمع ہے دیجور کی بمعنی المیلة المظلمة ( سیاہ رات) مكابد جمع مكبد بمعنی تکلیف ھو اجر جمع ہے ہاجرہ کی بمعنی سخت گرمی کی دو پہر " اقتناص اشتعال سے بمعنی شکار کرنا نازفا ختم کرنے والا علالہ " باقی ماندہ چیز " الجد " کوشش الغاية القصوى " دونوں کا ایک ہی معنی ہے انتہا امطت [؟] باب افعال سے ہٹانا ارتیاب بمعنی شک۔
علت تالیف کتاب
امر ثانی غرض شاری [؟] :۔ اس عبارت میں شارح نے علت تالیف کتاب (شرح) کو بیان کیا ہے لیکن اس کو سوال جواب کی شکل میں سمجھیں۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ جب تنقیح اتنی خوبیوں پر مشتمل تھی کہ یہ چھوٹی بڑی کتابوں کے خلاصہ کو شامل ہے اور اپنے ماسوا دوسری کتابوں سے بے پرواہ کرنے والی ہے تو پھر اس کی شرح لکھنے کی کیا ضرورت تھی؟ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ تنقیح اور توضیح انتہائی ادق کتاب تھی اس کی کوئی شرح نہ تھی لوگ اس کو حل کرنے کے لئے حواشی پر گزارہ کر رہے تھے جس کی وجہ سے ظاہری الفاظ تو سمجھ رہے تھے لیکن اس کے اندر جو نکات اور مضامین چھپے ہوئے تھے ان تک رسائی نہیں ہو رہی تھی اس لئے میں نے اس کی شرح لکھی تا کہ وہ نکات اور مضامین واضح ہو جائیں اور طلباء کی پریشانی دور ہو جائے اور علم کی پیاس بجھ جائے ۔
امر ثالث استعارات:۔ مصنف نے انتظار کو تشبیہ دی ہے اشخاص کے ساتھ تو ذکر مشبہ کا ہے مراد بھی مشبہ ہے اور وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے اس لئے لفظ انظار میں استعارہ مکیہ ہے اور اشخاص (مشبہ بہ ) کے لوازمات میں سے ان کی انگلیاں ہیں اس لئے انامل " میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے۔۔ اسی طرح معضلات کو تشبیہ دی ہے قیمتی سامان کی تھیلیوں کے ساتھ تو ذکر مشبہ کا ہے مراد بھی مشبہ ہے اور وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے لہذا یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہے ۔ اور قیمتی سامان کی تھیلیوں کے لوازمات میں سے گر ہیں ہیں اس لئے لفظ عقد میں استعارہ تخلیلیہ ہے اور تھیلوں کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کہ ان کو کھولا جائے تو ملا محل میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے نیز بیان کو تنبیہ دی ہے شخص کے ساتھ ذکر مشبہ کا مراد بھی مشبہ ہے تو لفظ بیان میں استعارہ مکیہ ہے شخص مشبہ بہ کے لوازمات میں سے پورے ہیں اس لئے بنان میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور اس کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کھولنا اس لئے فتح میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے۔ اسی طرح مغلقات کو تشبیہ دی ہے مکانوں کے ساتھ ذکر مشبہ کا مراد بھی مشبہ ہے تو مغلقات میں استعارہ مکنیہ ہے اور مکان مشبہ بہ ) کے لوازمات میں سے دروازے ہیں تو ابواب میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور مکان کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کہ دروازوں کو کھولا جائے تو ان پلیح، " میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے۔ اور خدائد ( معانی کتاب) کو تشبیہ دی ہے خوبصورت محبوباؤں کے ساتھ ذکر مشبہ بہ کا ہے اور مراد مشبہ ہے لہذا اخر ائد میں استعارہ تصریحیہ ہے، خیام خرائد کے لوازمات میں سے ہیں تو خیام میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور مقصورات مناسبات میں سے ہے تو مقصورات میں استعارہ ترشیحیہ ہے ہم کو تشبیہ دی ہے ذی اعناق کے ساتھ ذکر مشبہ کا مراد بھی مشبہ ہے اور وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے اس لئے ہم میں استعارہ مکنیہ ہے اور اعناق لوازمات میں سے ہیں لھذا اس میں استعارہ تخیلیہ اور استشراف مناسبات سے ہے تو مستشرفہ میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے۔
ثُمَّ جَمَعتُ هَذَا الشَّرحَ المَوْسُومَ بِالتَّلويح إِلَى كَشفِ حَفَانَقِ التَّنقِيحِ . مُشتَمِلا عَلَى تَقرير قَوَاعِدِ الفَنِّ وَتَحرِيرِ مَعَاقِدِهِ وَتَفسِيرِ مَقَاصِدِ الكِتَابِ وَتَكثِيرِ فَوَائِدِهِ مَعَ تَنقِيحٍ لِمَا آثَرَ فِيهِ المُصَنِّفُ بَسطَ الكَلَامِ وَتَوضِيحٍ لِمَا اقْتَصَرَ . فِيهِ عَلَى ضبطِ المَرَام فِى ضِمن تَقرِيرَاتٍ تَنفَتِحُ لِوُرُودِهَا أَصدَافُ الآذَانِ وَتَحقِيقَاتِ تَهْتَزُّ لِإدرَاكِهَا أَعْطَافُ الأذهَانِ وَتَوجيهاتٍ يَنشَطُ لِاسْتِمَاعِهَا الكَسَلانُ وَتَقسِيمَاتٍ يَطْرَبُ عِندَ سَمَاعِهَا الثَّكَلانُ مُعَوِّلًا فِي مُتُونَ الرِّوَايَةِ عَلَى مَا اسْتَهَرَ مِن الكتب الشَّرِيفَةِ وَمُعَرِّجًا فِي عُيُون الدِّرَايَةِ عَلَى مَا تَقَرَّرَ مِن النُّكَتِ اللَّطِيفَةِ وَسَيَجِدُ الغَائِصُ فِي بِحَارِ التَّحَقِيقِ الفَائِضُ عَلَيْهِ أَنوَارُ التَّوفِيقِ مَا أودَعتُ فِى هَذَا الكِتَابِ الَّذِى لَا يَستَكشِفُ القِنَاعَ عَن حَقَايْقِهِ إِلَّا المَاهِرُ مِن عُلَمَاءِ الْفَرِيقَينِ وَلَا يَستَاهِلُ لِلاطلاعِ عَلَى دَقَائِقِهِ إِلَّا الْبَارِعُ فِي أُصُولِ المَذهَبَينِ
Heading: Diving into the text – Farā'id is plural of farīdah meaning large pearl; Maṭwiyāt is plural of maṭwiyyah meaning folded thing; Rumūz is plural of ramz meaning sign; Masālik is plural of maslak meaning path; Shi‘āb is a difficult mountain pass; Shawārid is plural of shāridah meaning wild animal; Iqtaḥama, from ifta‘ala, meaning enters; Mawārid is plural of mawrid meaning place of arrival; Dayājū is plural of dayjūr meaning the dark night (black night); Makābid is plural of makbad meaning difficulty; Hājir is plural of hājirah meaning intense midday heat; Iqtināṣ, from isht‘āl, meaning hunting; Nāzifā: finisher; ‘Ulālah: leftover; Al-jadd: effort; Al-ghāyat al-quṣwā: both have the same meaning: extremity; Amatṭt [or Azalt?], from bāb al-af‘āl: remove; Irtiyāb: doubt.
Reason for writing the book
Second matter: The commentator's purpose: In this passage, the commentator has expressed the reason for writing the commentary (sharh), but understand it in the form of a question-answer. Question: Since al-Tanqīḥ was so excellent that it comprised the summary of small and large books and made one independent of other books, then what was the need to write its commentary? Answer: Al-Tanqīḥ and al-Tawḍīḥ were extremely subtle books; they had no commentary. People were relying on marginal notes to solve them, whereby they understood the outward words but could not access the hidden points and subjects within. Therefore I wrote this commentary so that those points and subjects become clear, the distress of students is removed, and the thirst for knowledge is quenched.
Third matter: Metaphors: The author likened 'waits' to persons: the mention is of the thing compared (mushabbah) and the intended is also the mushabbah, and the point of similarity is concealed in the mind, hence in the word anzār there is a makkiyyah (implicit) metaphor. And among the accessories of persons (the mushabbah bihi) are their fingers, so in the word anāmil there is a takhyīliyyah (suppositional) metaphor. Similarly, he likened 'difficulties' to bags of precious goods: the mention is of the mushabbah and the intended is the mushabbah, so it is a makkiyyah metaphor. And among the accessories of the bags are knots, so in the word ‘uqad there is a takhyīliyyah metaphor. And among the appropriates of the bags is that they are opened, so in the word maḥall there is a tarshīḥiyyah (strengthening) metaphor. Also, he likened 'bayān' (explanation) to a person: so in bayān there is a makkiyyah metaphor; among the accessories of the person are complete limbs? so in binān there is a takhyīliyyah metaphor; and among its appropriates is opening, so in fatḥ there is a tarshīḥiyyah metaphor. Similarly, he likened 'mughlaqāt' (closed things) to places: so in mughlaqāt there is a makniyyah (implicit) metaphor; among the accessories of places are doors, so in abwāb there is a takhyīliyyah metaphor; and among the appropriates of places is that doors are opened, so in anfataḥ? there is a tarshīḥiyyah metaphor. And he likened 'kharā'id' (meanings of the book) to beautiful beloved women: the mention is of the mushabbah bihi and the intended is the mushabbah, so in kharā'id there is a taṣrīḥiyyah (explicit) metaphor; among the accessories of beloved women are tents, so in khiyām there is a takhyīliyyah metaphor; and among the appropriates are secluded chambers, so in maqṣūrāt there is a tarshīḥiyyah metaphor. He likened 'hum' (them) to those with necks: so in hum there is a makniyyah metaphor; among the accessories are necks, so in a‘nāq there is a takhyīliyyah metaphor; and among the appropriates is looking up, so in mustashrifah there is a tarshīḥiyyah metaphor.
Then I compiled this commentary, named al-Talwīḥ, for uncovering the obscure points of al-Tanqīḥ, including the establishment of the rules of the discipline, the editing of its nodes, the explanation of the book's objectives, and the multiplication of its benefits, along with a revision of what the author chose to elaborate upon and clarification of what he limited himself to summarily. It comprises expositions at whose arrival the shells of ears open, verifications at whose understanding the sides of minds sway, directions that invigorate the lazy to listen, and classifications that delight the bereaved at hearing. Relying in the texts of transmission (riwāyah) on what is well-known from the noble books, and turning in the eyes of insight (dirāyah) to what is established from the subtle points. And the diver in the seas of investigation, upon whom the lights of success overflow, will find what I have deposited in this book, whose realities are not unveiled except by the expert from the scholars of both schools (of fiqh and usul?), and whose subtleties are not worthy of being accessed except by the proficient in the principles of the two madhhabs.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is from the front matter of the commentary 'al-Tarwīḥ' on 'al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ', a work on Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first lists several Arabic terms with their lexical meanings, serving as preparatory vocabulary. Then he discusses the reason for writing the commentary (ʿillat al-taʾlīf) in a question-and-answer format: despite the excellence of the original work (al-Tanqīḥ/al-Tawḍīḥ), it was extremely subtle and lacked a commentary, so students could only grasp the surface. The author wrote this commentary to uncover hidden points and relieve students' distress. Next, he analyzes the metaphors (istiʿārāt) used by the original author, categorizing them into types: makkiyyah (implicit), takhyīliyyah (suppositional), tarshīḥiyyah (strengthening), makniyyah, taṣrīḥiyyah (explicit), and others. Each example shows how the author creatively extended the original text's rhetoric to enhance understanding. Finally, a concluding Arabic paragraph describes the commentary's features: it establishes usul rules, clarifies objectives, and is intended only for advanced scholars. This front matter establishes the commentary's purpose and scholarly method.

Key Terms
علت تالیف (ʿillat al-taʾlīf): The reason or motivating cause for composing the book.
شرح (sharḥ): Commentary; a detailed explanation of a text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what was the primary shortcoming of al-Tanqīḥ and al-Tawḍīḥ that necessitated a commentary?
A) They contained many errors.
B) They were too lengthy and needed abridgment.
C) They were extremely subtle and lacked any existing commentary to unlock their inner meanings.
D) They were written in a dialect not understood by students.

Key Takeaway
A commentary is needed when a text's depth is not self-evident; the commentator's role is to unveil hidden meanings and relieve student confusion.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Decoding the Metaphors in the Commentary
Author classifies and explains each metaphor in the original text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the types of metaphors (makniyya, takhyiliyya, tashrihiyya, tasrihiyya) used by the author and explain their function in elucidating the original usul text.

Core Idea
The author uses a systematic rhetorical analysis to unlock layered meanings in the original text through metaphor classification.

This passage presents the author's detailed metaphorical analysis of the original author's language. He takes each metaphorical expression in the original text, identifies the mushabbah (thing compared) and mushabbah bihi (thing compared to), and categorizes the type of isti'āra (metaphor) involved. This rhetorical dissection is part of his larger project to expose the hidden layers of meaning in al-Tanqīḥ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six metaphorical groups
The author discusses six groups: (1) anzār (waits), (2) mu‘ḍilāt (difficulties), (3) bayān (explanation), (4) mughlaqāt (closed things), (5) kharā’id (meanings), (6) hum (them). For each, note the central simile.
These correspond to key terms in the original text.
2
Classify the primary metaphor type for each group
For each group, determine if the metaphor is makniyya (implicit - mushabbah mentioned, mushabbah bihi implied) or tasrihiyya (explicit - mushabbah bihi mentioned). The author states, e.g., for anzār it is makniyya; for kharā’id it is tasrihiyya.
Makniyya leaves the comparison implicit; tasrihiyya states it outright.
3
Identify the takhyīliyya (suppositional) metaphor
The author points out ancillary words (e.g., anāmil 'fingers' for persons) that are accessories of the mushabbah bihi. These are takhyīliyya: they imagine a detail that belongs to the thing compared to.
This step shows how the metaphor is extended.
4
Identify the tarshīḥiyya (strengthening) metaphor
The author also notes words that are appropriate concomitants (e.g., maḥall 'place of opening' for bags). These are tarshīḥiyya: they strengthen the metaphor by adding a pertinent detail.
Tarshīḥiyya makes the metaphor more vivid.
5
Assess the pedagogical function
Understand that this classification is not mere literary exercise; it reveals how the original author used language to convey complex usul concepts indirectly. The commentary unpacks these to prevent confusion.
The rhetorical analysis is part of the 'clarification of hidden points' mentioned in the previous lesson.
